Three Methods of Resolving Ta'arud in Hanafi Usul
Explains three methods to resolve textual conflicts in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three Hanafi methods of resolving textual conflict (ta'arud) — carrying to different aspects, different situations, and abrogation (naskh) — to derive rulings from conflicting proofs.

Core Idea
Hanafi usul first reconciles conflicting proofs by harmonizing (jam‘); only when chronology is certain and reconciliation impossible does abrogation apply.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar introduces the core Hanafi approach to apparent contradictions between legal proofs. Unlike some madhabs that quickly resort to abrogation or preference, the Hanafi method first exhausts all possibilities of harmonization (jam‘) by applying each proof to a different aspect or situation. Only when chronological priority is certain does abrogation (naskh) become necessary. In this lesson, we will work through three key examples: the two verses on oaths, the two readings of Surah al-Baqarah on menstruation, and the abrogation of the widow's iddah by the pregnant woman's iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting proofs
Locate the two texts (verses or qira'at) that appear to contradict each other. Note their apparent implications.
In the oath example: al-Baqarah 2:225 and al-Ma'idah 5:89.
2
Check if reconciliation by aspect (haml 'ala jiha) is possible
Can each proof be assigned to a different dimension of the ruling? Hanafis do this by interpreting one proof as addressing otherworldly consequences and the other as addressing worldly obligations.
For oaths: al-Baqarah → sin in afterlife; al-Ma'idah → expiation in this world.
3
Check if reconciliation by situation (haml 'ala hal) is possible
Can each proof be applied to a distinct factual scenario? This is used for the qira'at on menstruation: one reading applies to maximum period, the other to shorter period.
Maximum menstruation is 10 days Hanafi view.
4
If chronology is known and reconciliation fails, apply naskh
When one verse is known to be revealed later and conflict is irreconcilable, the later abrogates the earlier. Example: the iddah of pregnant widow (Surah al-Talaq 65:4) abrogates the earlier verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:234) for that specific case.
Naskh is a last resort after jam‘ is exhausted.
5
Derive the final ruling
After applying the appropriate method, state the ruling that follows from the reconciled proofs. This is the mufta bihi position.
Hanafi position: no expiation for yamin ghamus; bathing required for purity if period ends before 10 days; pregnant widow's iddah ends at childbirth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التعارض بيان وقوع التعارض بين القياسين فلما تعارضت الآيتان في حق الغموس حملنا آية البقرة على المؤاخذة الأخروية، وآية المائدة على المؤاخذة الدنيوية فعلم أن في الغموس مؤاخذة أخروية، وهي الإثم لا مؤاخذة دنيوية، وهي الكفّارة وقد حرّرت فيما سبق بأطول من هذا. ومن قبل الحال بأن يحمل أحدهما على حالة والآخر على حالة كما في قوله تعالى: النصين، يَطْهُرْنَ بالتخفيف والتشديد، فإن في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ﴾ قرأ بعضهم يطهرن بالتخفيف، أي لا تقربوا الحائضات حتى يطهرن بانقطاع دمهن سواء اغتسلن أو لا، وقرأ بعضهم يَطَّهَّرْنَ بالتشديد، أي لا تقربوهن حتى يغتسلن، فتعارض بين القراءتين، وهما بمنزلة آيتين، فوجب التطبيق بينهما بأن تحمل قراءة التخفيف على ما إذا انقطع لعشرة أيام؛ إذ لا يحتمل الحيض المزيد على هذا، فمجرد انقطاع الدم حينئذٍ يُحِلَّ الوطء، وتحمل قراءة التشديد على ما إذا انقطع لأقل من عشرة أيام؛ إذ يحتمل عود الدم، فلا يؤكد انقطاعه إلا أن يغتسل. (القمر) تعارضت الآيتان إلخ وقد يقال إن المراد بكسب القلب في البقرة كسبه كذبًا، فإنه ليس المؤاخذة في كل كسب القلب صادقًا كان أو كاذبًا، وكسب القلب كذبًا ليس إلا في الغموس فإن في المنعقدة ليس كسب الكذب بل الصدق فيها في يد الحالف واختياره، والمراد في سورة المائدة بمَا عَقَدْتُمُ الْأَيْمَانَ اليمين المنعقدة، والمراد من المؤاخذة في كلتا الآيتين المؤاخذة الأخروية، فالمنعقدة مسكوت عنها في البقرة، والغموس مسكوت عنه في المائدة، فلا تعارض (القمر) حملنا آية البقرة إلخ فإن المؤاخذة في آية البقرة مطلقة، والمطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل، وهو المؤاخذة الأخروية (القمر) على المؤاخذة إلخ بدليل قوله تعالى: فَكَفَّارَتُه الآية، فإن الكفارة في دار الكفارة (القمر) وقد حرّرت إلخ أي في مبحث الحقيقة والمجاز.(القمر) حتى يطهرن بانقطاع إلخ : فبعد الطهارة قبل الغسل يَحِلّ الوطء. (القمر) حتى يغتسلن: فبعد الطهارة قبل الغسل يحرم الوطء . (القمر) يحل الوطء: إذا لم يبق كان سبب حرمة الوطء. (القمر) عود الدم إلخ : فإن غاية مدّة الحيض عشرة أيام. (القمر) إلا أن يغتسل إلخ الأصوب أن يقول: إلا أن يغتسل أو يمضي عليها زمن يسع الغسل ولبس الثياب والتحريمة، وهذا فيما إذا طهرت في وقت بقي منه إلى خروجه قدر الاغتسال ولبس الثياب والتحريمة كذا قال الطحطاوي، والسرّ أنه لما مضت مدةٌ تَسَعُ الغسل والتحريمة ولبس الثياب وجبت عليها الصلاة فصارت طاهرة في نظر الشارع، فيحل الوطء أيضًا. (القمر) الأذى، وهو (القمر) أو يمضي عليها وقت صلاة كاملة ليحكم بطهارتها، ولكن يرد عليه أن قوله تعالى: فَإِذَا تَطَهَّرْنَ فَأْتُوهُنَّ ، بعد ذلك ليس إلا بالتشديد، فهو يؤكد جهة الاغتسال على التقديرين إلا أن يقال: يدلّ على استحباب الغسل دون الوجوب، أو يحمل "تطهرن" أي قبل الوطء حينئذٍ على طَهَّرْنَ كَ تَبَيَّنَ بمعنى بَانَ. أو من قبل اختلاف الزمان صريحًا، فإنه إذا علم التاريخ فلا بد أن يكون المتأخر ناسخا للمتقدّم كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُولاتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ أَنْ يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ﴾ نزلت بعد الآية التي في سورة البقرة ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنْكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجاً يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنْفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْراً﴾ فإن هذه الآية تدل على أن عدة متوفى الزوج أربعة أشهر وعشر سواء كانت حاملة أو لا، والآية الأولى تدلّ على أن عدّة الحامل وضع الحمل سواء كانت مطلقة أو متوفى الزوج، فبينهما عموم وخصوص من وجه، فتعارض بينهما في المادة الاجتماعية، وهي الحامل المتوفى عنها زوجها، ولكن يرد عليه إلخ قلت في جوابه إن تأكيد آية وترجيحها لا يحصل بآية أخرى؛ لأنه يفضي إلى الترجيح بكثرة الأدلة، وذلك لا يجوز، بل يحصل الترجيح بقوة الأدلة وهي لم توجد ههنا؛ لأن كليهما آيتان، وهذا التأويل الذي قالت الحنفية به في هذه الآية أولى مما ذهب إليه الشافعي من لزوم الكفارة في القسمين أي والمنعقدة، ووجه أولوية تأويلنا أن تأويله يوجب أن يكون سائر ذنب الحنث في المنعقدة، وسائر ذنب الغموس الذي هو الكبيرة المحضة واحدا، وهو خلاف قانون الشرع، وأيضًا يلزم أن يكون الغموس أسهل بحيث يأخذ مال مسلم، ويحلف كاذبًا عمدًا، ثم يكفّر ويطهر من دنس ذنبه (السنبلي) الغموس جهة الاغتسال إلخ فقبل الاغتسال يحرم الوطء على كلا التقديرين. (القمر) التقديرين: أي على تقدير انقطاع الحيض بعشرة أيام وتقدير انقطاع الحيض لأقل من عشرة أيام. (القمر) أو يحمل إلخ فإن "تفعل" قد يكون بمعنى "فَعَل". (القمر) فبينهما : أي بين الآيتين عموم وخصوص من وجه، فغير الحامل المتوفّى الزوج يشملها آية سورة البقرة لا آية سورة الطلاق والحامل المطلقة يشملها آية سورة الطلاق لا آية سورة البقرة، والحامل المتوفّى عنها زوجها يشملها كلتا الآيتين.(القمر)
Chapter on Conflict: Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two analogies. When the two verses conflicted regarding the false oath (ghamus), we carried the verse of al-Baqarah to mean otherworldly punishment, and the verse of al-Ma'idah to mean worldly punishment. So it is known that in the false oath there is otherworldly punishment, which is sin, not worldly punishment, which is expiation. And I have elaborated on this previously in more detail. And by way of situation: by carrying one of them to one situation and the other to another situation, as in His statement: the two texts, 'yathurna' with tashdid and without. For in His statement {And do not approach them until they are pure} some read 'yathurna' without tashdid, meaning do not approach menstruating women until they are purified by the cessation of their blood, whether they have bathed or not. And some read 'yattahharna' with tashdid, meaning do not approach them until they bathe. So there is conflict between the two readings, and they are like two verses. So harmonization between them is necessary by carrying the reading without tashdid to the case when the blood stops at ten days, since menstruation cannot exceed that, so mere cessation of blood then makes intercourse lawful. And carry the reading with tashdid to the case when it stops at less than ten days, since the blood may return, so its cessation is not assured unless she bathes. (al-Qamar) The two verses conflicted etc. It may be said that what is meant by 'earnings of the heart' in al-Baqarah is earning falsehood, for punishment is not for every earning of the heart, whether truthful or false. Earning falsehood only occurs in the false oath (ghamus), while in the sworn oath (mun'aqida) there is no earning of falsehood, rather truthfulness is in the hand and choice of the swearer. And what is meant in Surah al-Ma'idah by {the oaths you swear} (5:89) is the sworn oath. And what is meant by punishment in both verses is otherworldly punishment. Thus the sworn oath is left unmentioned in al-Baqarah, and the false oath is left unmentioned in al-Ma'idah, so there is no conflict. (al-Qamar) We carried the verse of al-Baqarah etc. For the punishment in the verse of al-Baqarah is absolute, and the absolute is carried to the complete, which is otherworldly punishment. (al-Qamar) To the punishment etc. by the evidence of His statement {the expiation for it} (5:89), for expiation is in the abode of expiation. (al-Qamar) And I have elaborated etc. i.e. in the discussion of truth and metaphor. (al-Qamar) Until they are purified by cessation etc.: So after purification before bathing, intercourse is lawful. (al-Qamar) Until they bathe: So after purification before bathing, intercourse is prohibited. (al-Qamar) Makes intercourse lawful: When the cause for prohibition of intercourse no longer exists. (al-Qamar) The blood may return etc.: For the maximum duration of menstruation is ten days. (al-Qamar) Unless she bathes etc. The more correct is to say: Unless she bathes or a time passes sufficient for bathing, wearing clothes, and the opening takbir. This applies when she becomes pure at a time such that there remains until its end enough time for bathing, wearing clothes, and the opening takbir. So said al-Tahtawi. The reason is that when a period sufficient for bathing, the opening takbir, and wearing clothes has passed, prayer becomes obligatory on her, so she becomes pure in the view of the Lawgiver, and thus intercourse is also lawful. (al-Qamar) Harm, which is (al-Qamar) Or a complete prayer time passes to rule her purity. But it is objected to that His statement {Then when they have purified themselves, come to them} (2:222) is only with tashdid, so it emphasizes the aspect of bathing on both assumptions, unless it is said that it indicates the recommendation of bathing, not obligation, or that 'tatahharna' here before intercourse means 'tahharna' like 'tabayyana' in the sense of 'bana' (became clear). Or by explicit difference in time: when the date is known, then the later must be abrogating the earlier, as in His statement {And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth} (65:4) which was revealed after the verse in al-Baqarah {And those of you who die and leave wives behind, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days} (2:234). For this verse indicates that the 'iddah of a woman whose husband dies is four months and ten days, whether she is pregnant or not. And the first verse indicates that the 'iddah of a pregnant woman is childbirth, whether she is divorced or a widow. Between them is 'umum wa khusus min wajh', so they conflict in the common ground, which is the pregnant widow. But it is objected etc. I said in response: Confirmation and preference of one verse over another cannot be achieved by another verse, because it leads to preference by multiplicity of proofs, which is not permissible. Rather, preference is achieved by strength of proofs, and that is not present here, because both are verses. This interpretation that the Hanafis have held regarding this verse is preferable to what al-Shafi'i went to of requiring expiation in both types (i.e., the sworn oath). The reason for the preference of our interpretation is that his interpretation would make the rest of the sin of breaking the sworn oath and the rest of the sin of the false oath, which is purely a major sin, equal, which is contrary to the law of the Shari'a. Also, it would require that the false oath be easier: one takes a Muslim's property and swears falsely intentionally, then makes expiation and becomes pure from the filth of his sin. (al-Sunbuli) The false oath: Aspect of bathing etc.: So before bathing, intercourse is prohibited on both assumptions. (al-Qamar) The two assumptions: i.e., assumption of cessation of menstruation at ten days and assumption of cessation of menstruation at less than ten days. (al-Qamar) Or it is carried etc.: For 'taf'al' may come in the meaning of 'fa'ala'. (al-Qamar) Between them: i.e., between the two verses is 'umum wa khusus min wajh': the non-pregnant widow is covered by the verse of al-Baqarah but not by the verse of al-Talaq; the pregnant divorcee is covered by the verse of al-Talaq but not by the verse of al-Baqarah; the pregnant widow is covered by both verses. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Ta'arud (conflict) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains three methods of resolving textual conflict when two proofs (Quranic verses or hadith) appear contradictory. The first method is to apply each proof to a different aspect of the issue. For example, regarding the oath called yamin ghamus (false oath deliberately), the verse in Surah al-Baqarah (2:225) 'He will not take you to task for what is unintentional in your oaths' is interpreted as referring to otherworldly punishment (sin), while the verse in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:89) 'God will not take you to task for what is unintentional in your oaths' is interpreted as referring to worldly punishment (expiation). Thus there is no real conflict: both address different aspects. The author notes that this reconciliation avoids the unacceptable consequence of equating a major sin (ghamus) with a minor expiable sin (mun'aqida). The second method is to apply the conflicting proofs to different factual situations. This is illustrated by the two variant readings of the word 'yathurna' in Surah al-Baqarah (2:222). One reading (without tashdid) means 'until they become pure' (i.e., menstrual flow stops), while the other (with tashdid) means 'until they bathe.' The Hanafis reconcile by applying the first to a woman whose period ends at ten days (the maximum), after which mere cessation allows intercourse, and the second to a woman whose period ends before ten days, where bathing is required because blood may return. The third method is abrogation (naskh) when the chronological order is known. For example, the verse on the 'iddah of pregnant women (Surah al-Talaq 65:4) was revealed after the verse on the 'iddah of widows (Surah al-Baqarah 2:234). The later verse abrogates the earlier in the case of a pregnant widow, so her 'iddah is until childbirth, not four months and ten days. The author also criticizes the Shafi'i position that both types of oaths require expiation, arguing it leads to unacceptable consequences.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'āruḍ): The apparent conflict between two legal proofs (adilla) that cannot both be applied simultaneously without reconciliation.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a prior ruling by a later revealed ruling when chronological order is known and reconciliation is impossible.
القراءات (al-qirā'āt): The variant canonical readings of the Quran, each considered a divine revelation. In usul, they are treated as separate textual evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi resolution of the conflict between the two verses on oaths (al-Baqarah 2:225 and al-Ma'idah 5:89), what is the ruling on yamin ghamus (false oath)?
A) It requires expiation (kaffarah) in this world.
B) It results only in sin (ithm) in the afterlife, with no worldly expiation.
C) It is forgiven entirely unless it involves taking property.
D) It requires both expiation and repentance.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul resolves proof conflicts by first seeking reconciliation (jam‘) through aspect or situation; only when chronology is certain and reconciliation impossible does naskh apply.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
Resolving Ta'arud Between 'Iddah Verses via Naskh
Resolving ta'arud via naskh with chronological evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school resolves the apparent conflict between Quran 2:234 and Quran 65:4 using the principle of naskh, identifying the chronological evidence and its implications.

Core Idea
The later revelation (Surah At-Talaq) abrogates the earlier (Al-Baqarah) for the pregnant widow; 'iddah ends with childbirth.

This passage examines a classic case of ta'arud (apparent conflict) between two Quranic verses governing the 'iddah period. Surah Al-Baqarah (2:234) prescribes four months and ten days for widows without mention of pregnancy, while Surah At-Talaq (65:4) states that the 'iddah of a pregnant woman ends with childbirth. The overlap is the pregnant widow, creating a conflict that must be resolved. The Hanafi solution relies on the principle of naskh (abrogation) based on knowledge of the chronological order of revelation, as transmitted by the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting verses
Locate the exact texts: Quran 2:234 (four months ten days for widows) and Quran 65:4 ('iddah ends with childbirth for pregnant women). Note that they are both Quranic (qat'i al-thubut) and appear to give different rulings for the pregnant widow.
The verses are: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days' (2:234) and 'And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth to their burden' (65:4).
2
Analyze the relationship between the two texts
Determine the 'general-specific from one aspect' (umum wa khusus min wajh) relationship. The Baqarah verse covers all widows (pregnant or not); the Talaq verse covers all pregnant women (divorced or widowed). Their intersection is the pregnant widow, where the rulings conflict.
The Hanafi commentator explains: non-pregnant widow covered only by Baqarah; pregnant divorced woman covered only by Talaq; pregnant widow covered by both.
3
Apply the principle of naskh based on chronological order
The text states that the Talaq verse was revealed after the Baqarah verse. Knowledge of this order comes from transmitted reports (riwaya), particularly from Ibn Mas'ud and the practice of Umar. Since the later revelation abrogates the earlier in the scope of the overlap, the Talaq verse governs the pregnant widow: her 'iddah ends with childbirth.
Ibn Mas'ud is reported to have said: 'Whoever wishes, I will imprecate him that Surah an-Nisa' al-Qusra (i.e., At-Talaq) was revealed after the four months and ten days.'
4
Identify the opposing position and the Hanafi response
Some early scholars (e.g., Ali, according to one opinion) held that the pregnant widow should observe the longer of the two periods (ab'adal-ajalain) as a precaution, due to uncertainty about which verse is later. The Hanafi response is that the chronology is firmly established through naql (transmission) and the consensus of Companions like Umar, so naskh is valid.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): under the Hanafi view, a widow who gives birth a week after her husband's death may remarry immediately; under the precautionary view, she must wait four months and ten days.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The text concludes that both Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i adopted the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud and Umar, making childbirth the end of the 'iddah for a pregnant widow. This is the relied-upon position.
This is a rare case of agreement between the two schools (muttafaq alayh).

Chapter on Conflict: Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two analogies. Or a complete prayer time passes over her to rule on her purity, but it is objected that His statement: 'When they have purified themselves, then come to them' (Quran 2:222) after that is only with emphasis, so it emphasizes the aspect of washing on both estimates, except that it may be said: it indicates the recommendation of washing, not obligation, or one interprets 'tatahharna' (before intercourse) as 'tahhara' like 'tabayyana' meaning 'bana'. Or due to difference of time explicitly, for when the date is known, the later must abrogate the earlier, like His statement: 'And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth to their burden' (Quran 65:4) was revealed after the verse in Surah Al-Baqarah: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days' (Quran 2:234). For this verse indicates that the 'iddah of a woman whose husband dies is four months and ten days, whether she is pregnant or not, and the first verse indicates that the 'iddah of a pregnant woman is the delivery of her burden, whether she is divorced or her husband died. So between them is general and specific from one aspect, so there is conflict in the social matter, namely the pregnant woman whose husband died. But it is objected... I said in its answer that confirming a verse and giving it preponderance cannot be obtained by another verse, because it leads to preponderance by multiplicity of evidences, and that is not permissible. Rather, preponderance is obtained by strength of evidences, which are not found here, because both are verses. And this interpretation by the Hanafis in this verse is more appropriate than what al-Shafi'i went to of the necessity of expiation in both categories, i.e., the confirmed (oath). The superiority of our interpretation is that his interpretation would make the residue of the sin of the broken confirmed oath and the residue of the sin of the deliberate false oath, which is the major sin, one and the same, which is contrary to the law of the Shari'ah. Also, it would make the deliberate false oath easier, to the extent that one takes a Muslim's property and deliberately swears falsely, then expiates and is purified from the filth of his sin. (al-Sanbali) The deliberate false oath. The aspect of washing etc.: before washing, intercourse is forbidden on both estimates. (al-Qamar) The two estimates: i.e., on the estimate of the cessation of menstruation at ten days and the estimate of cessation of menstruation at less than ten days. (al-Qamar) Or one interprets etc.: for 'taf'alu' may be in the meaning of 'fa'ala'. (al-Qamar) Between them: i.e., between the two verses is general and specific from one aspect: the non-pregnant woman whose husband died is covered by the verse of Surah Al-Baqarah, not by the verse of Surah At-Talaq; the pregnant divorced woman is covered by the verse of Surah At-Talaq, not by the verse of Surah Al-Baqarah; and the pregnant woman whose husband died is covered by both verses. (al-Qamar) Chapter on Conflict: Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two analogies. Therefore he (Ali) says: She observes the longer of the two periods as a precaution: if childbirth is near, she observes four months and ten days; if childbirth is far, she observes it due to lack of knowledge of the date. And Ibn Mas'ud said: She observes by giving birth. And he argued against Ali: Whoever wishes, I will imprecate him that Surah an-Nisa' al-Qusra, i.e., Surah At-Talaq which contains His statement: 'And those who are pregnant' was revealed after that in Surah Al-Baqarah. So when the date is known, His statement: 'And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth to their burden' (65:4) abrogates His statement: 'And those of you who die' (2:234) in the scope of what they both covered, so act by it. And thus Umar said: 'If she gives birth while her husband is on the bed (i.e., not yet buried), her 'iddah ends, and it becomes lawful for her to marry.' And Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i both adopted this. Or by indication, coordinating with his statement 'explicitly': i.e., due to difference of time by indication, like the prohibitor and the permitter: when they combine in a ruling, they act on the prohibitor and consider it later in indication than the permitter. The two periods: i.e., the term of the 'iddah of death and the term of the 'iddah of pregnancy. (al-Muhashi) 'Due to lack of knowledge etc.' is attached to his statement 'he says'. (al-Qamar) 'And he argued etc.' narrated by Imam Muhammad and Ali did not deny it, as said by Ibn al-Malak. (al-Qamar) 'Whoever wishes, I will imprecate him etc.' reported in the Sunan with chain to Masruq from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Al-Aini said: Al-mubahalah is derived from al-bahl, meaning cursing. They used to say when they differed on something: 'May the curse of Allah be upon the liar among us.' It is said it is legislated in our time as well, as in al-Aini. (al-Sanbali) Al-bahl, al-mubahalah: the people gather when they differ on something and say: 'The curse of Allah be upon the oppressor among us.' (al-Qamar) 'In the scope of what they both covered' which is the situation of the woman whose husband died. This statement is attached to his statement 'abrogating'. (al-Qamar) 'By indication': i.e., what is established by transmitted report explicitly, but evidence indicates the time is different. Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis from a Hanafi usul work, likely the commentary (sharh) of 'Nur al-Anwar', discussing how to resolve an apparent conflict (ta'arud) between two Quranic verses regarding the 'iddah of a pregnant widow. The two verses are Surah Al-Baqarah 2:234, which sets the 'iddah of a widow at four months and ten days without mentioning pregnancy, and Surah At-Talaq 65:4, which states that the 'iddah of a pregnant woman ends with childbirth. The commentator explains that these verses have a general-specific relationship (umum wa khusus min wajh): the Baqarah verse applies to all widows (pregnant or not), while the Talaq verse applies to all pregnant women (divorced or widowed). Their overlap is the pregnant widow, causing an apparent contradiction. The resolution, according to the text, is based on knowledge of the chronological order of revelation: the Talaq verse was revealed later, so it abrogates (nasikh) the Baqarah verse specifically for the case of the pregnant widow. Thus, the pregnant widow's 'iddah ends with childbirth, as held by Ibn Mas'ud and Umar, and adopted by both Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i. The passage also includes a digression into a dispute with al-Shafi'i about the kaffarah for breaking oaths (al-yamin al-ghamus vs al-mun'aqidah), but the main focus remains on the principle of naskh based on textual chronology.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'āruḍ): The apparent conflict or contradiction between two legal evidences that seem to give opposite rulings.
الناسخ (al-nāsikh): The later revelation that abrogates the earlier ruling for the specific case of the pregnant widow.
عدة الحامل (ʻiddat al-ḥāmil): The waiting period for a pregnant woman after divorce or death of husband; ends with childbirth according to the later revelation.
عموم وخصوص من وجه (ʻumūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh): A relationship where two texts are general in one aspect and specific in another, overlapping in one instance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi method presented in the passage, what resolves the apparent conflict between Surah Al-Baqarah 2:234 and Surah At-Talaq 65:4 regarding the 'iddah of a pregnant widow?
A) Both verses are given equal weight, and the longer period is always observed.
B) The later verse (65:4) abrogates the earlier (2:234) for the pregnant widow, so her 'iddah ends with childbirth.
C) The earlier verse (2:234) is considered stronger because it is more general.
D) The verses are reconciled by applying the Baqarah verse to divorced women and the Talaq verse to widows.

Key Takeaway
When two Quranic verses conflict on a specific case, knowledge of the chronological order of revelation allows the later verse to abrogate the earlier, resolving the ta'arud.

Naskh — Abrogation

Naskh as Bayan Tabdeel: Clarification and Substitution
Definition of Naskh as Bayan Tabdeel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul defines naskh as both clarification (bayan) and substitution (tabdeel), and identify the basis of the dispute with Shams al-A'imma.

Core Idea
Naskh is a clarification of the ruling's hidden time limit from Allah's perspective, but a substitution from our perspective.

This passage examines the dual nature of naskh by linking the Quranic terms 'tabdeel' and 'naskh'. It argues that abrogation is not an arbitrary change but a revelation of the pre-eternal time limit of the ruling. This leads to a subtle intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether naskh qualifies as a division of bayan. We will unpack the reasoning and the scholarly objection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Quranic evidence
Identify the two verses cited (16:101 and 2:106). Note how the author equates 'tabdeel' and 'naskh' to show they are conceptually one.
The conjunction creates a conceptual link: substitution is abrogation and vice versa.
2
Differentiate the two perspectives
The same event is bayan (clarification) for Allah because He always knew the ruling's limit, and tabdeel (substitution) for humans who perceived the ruling as perpetual.
This dual classification is the core of the definition.
3
Analyze the wine example
Work through the example: initial absolute permission of wine, then prohibition. In human understanding, permission seemed eternal; the prohibition felt like a change. For Allah, the prohibition merely revealed the pre-set expiry.
The example illustrates the concept of 'hukm mutlaq' (absolute ruling).
4
Grasp the objection of Shams al-A'imma
He argues that naskh is not a division of bayan because bayan benefits humans (to clarify what is hidden), while to Allah nothing is hidden. Naskh is simply removal of a ruling.
This objection raises a fundamental point about the purpose of bayan.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: whether naskh is included in works on bayan or treated separately. This affects the classification of usul topics.
The passage accommodates both views, but the standard Hanafi position includes naskh as a type of bayan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو بيان تبديل عطف على قوله بيان ضرورة، وهو النسخ في اللغة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا بَدَّلْنَا آيَةً مَكَانَ آيَةٍ﴾ ثم قال: ﴿مَا نَنْسَخْ مِنْ آيَةٍ أَوْ تُنْسِهَا﴾، فعلم أنهما واحد ومعنى بيان التبديل أنه بيان من وجه وتبديل من وجه على ما قال، وهو أي التبديل والنسخ بيان لمدة الحكم المطلق الذي كان معلومًا عند الله، إلا أنه أطلق، فصار ظاهره البقاء في حق البشر، يعني أن الله تعالى أباح الخمر مثلاً في أول الإسلام، وكان في علمه أن يحرمها بعد مدة ألبتة، ولكن لم يقل منا: إني أُبيح الخمر إلى مدة معينة بل أطلق الإباحة، فكان في زعمنا أنه تبقى هذه الإباحة إلى يوم القيامة، ثم لما جاء التحريم بعد ذلك مفاجأةً فكان تبديلا في حقنا؛ لأنه بدل الإباحة بالحرمة بيانًا محضا في حق صاحب الشرع لميعاد الإباحة الذي كان في علمه، فكونه بياناً في حق الله تعالى وكونه تبديلًا في حق البشر، قال القمر: ما ننسخ ما شرطية، ننسخ من آية أي نزل حكمها أو نُنسِها أي نمحيها من قلبك أو نؤخّرها فلا نزل حكمها ونرفع تلاوتها، أو نؤخرها في اللوح المحفوظ، وفي قراءة بلا همز من النسيان أي ننسها ونمحها من قلبك. قال السنبلي: والنسخ في اللغة مشترك بين الإزالة والنقل، وقيل: الإزالة معنى حقيقي له، والنقل مجازي، وقيل بالعكس، وقيل بالتواطي ومنه المناسخة لنقل السهام الموروثة من ورثة الميت إلى ورثته والتناسخ لانتقال الروح من بدن إلى بدن آخر، وفي الاصطلاح قيل: رفع الشارع الحكم الشرعي، زاد ابن الحاجب بدليل شرعي متأخر أخرج بالقيد الأول رفعه بالموت والنوم والغفلة وبالثاني فحوصل إلى آخر الشهر، فيخرج رفع مباح الأصل لو تحقق فإنه ليس بخطاب، ويخرج كل تخصيص؛ لأنه رفع للحكم من الابتداء، كذا قال بحر العلوم. قال القمر: الحكم المطلق: أي الغير المقيد بالتأبيد أو التوقيت فإن حكمه الذي كان إلخ معنى العبارة الحكم الذي كان تقييده بمدةٍ معلومًا عند الله تعالى وهذا التوجه أولى مما اختاره بحر العلوم من أن قول المصنف له الذي إلخ صفة للمدة. قال القمر: إلا أنه أطلقه أي ما قيد الحكم بالمدة. قال القمر: فكان في زعمنا إلخ لدلالة الإطلاق على البقاء. قال المحشي: حقنا فصار من هذا الوجه تبديلاً. قال القمر: بيانًا محضًا أي ليس فيه معنى التبديل. قال المحشي: الشرع: فصار من هذا الوجه بياناً. قال القمر: في حق الله تعالى إلخ فيه أن البيان ما هو بالنسبة إلى العباد، وأما بالنسبة إلى الله تعالى فجميع الأشياء ظاهرة ومعلومة له تعالى فلا ينبغي أن يُعدّ النسخ من أقسام البيان، بل هو رفع الحكم بعد ثبوته، ولذا لم يجعل شمس الأئمة النسخ من أقسام البيان.
Or Bayan Tabdeel: It is a conjunction on his saying 'Bayan Darura', and it is Naskh in language. Allah Almighty said: 'And when We substitute one verse in place of another' (16:101) and then said: 'Whatever verse We abrogate or cause to be forgotten' (2:106). So it is known that they are one. And the meaning of Bayan Tabdeel is that it is a clarification from one perspective and a substitution from another perspective, as he said. And it, i.e., substitution and abrogation, is a clarification of the period of the absolute ruling that was known with Allah, except that He gave it absolutely, so its apparent meaning became everlasting with respect to humans. For example, Allah Almighty permitted wine in early Islam, and it was in His knowledge that He would prohibit it after a period absolutely, but He did not say: 'I permit wine for a specific period' but rather gave the permission absolutely. So in our assumption, this permission would remain until the Day of Resurrection. Then when the prohibition came afterwards suddenly, it was a substitution from our perspective because it replaced permission with prohibition. It is a pure clarification from the perspective of the Lawgiver concerning the time of permission that was in His knowledge. So it is a clarification with respect to Allah Almighty and a substitution with respect to humans. Al-Qamar said: 'Ma nansakh – ma is conditional, nansakh min aya means We remove its ruling or nunsiha means We erase it from your heart, or delay it so We do not reveal its ruling and raise its recitation, or delay it in the Preserved Tablet. In one reading without hamz from nisyan meaning We make it forgotten and erase it from your heart.' Al-Sanbli said: 'Naskh linguistically is shared between removal and transfer. It is said removal is its real meaning, transfer metaphorical, or vice versa, or used by common consent. From it is al-munasakha for transferring inherited shares from the deceased's heirs to his heirs, and al-tanasukh for the transfer of a soul from one body to another. Terminologically it is said: The Lawgiver's removal of a legal ruling, with Ibn al-Hajib adding: by a later legal evidence. The first qualification excludes removal by death, sleep, or forgetfulness; the second excludes [the ruling's] expiry at the end of a month. Thus removal of an originally permissible act, if it occurred, would be excluded because it is not a command, and every specification is excluded because it is removal of the ruling from the beginning. Thus said Bahr al-Ulum.' Al-Qamar said: 'The absolute ruling: that which is not restricted by perpetuity or time, and its ruling that was... the meaning of the phrase is the ruling whose restriction to a period was known with Allah Almighty, and this interpretation is more appropriate than what Bahr al-Ulum chose, that the author's saying 'which was' is an attribute of the period.' Al-Qamar said: 'Except that he gave it absolutely i.e., he did not restrict the ruling to a period.' Al-Qamar said: 'So it was in our assumption etc., due to the absolute expression indicating continuance.' Al-Muhashi said: 'Our perspective: so it became from this perspective a substitution.' Al-Qamar said: 'Pure clarification i.e., no meaning of substitution in it.' Al-Muhashi said: 'The Lawgiver: so it became from this perspective a clarification.' Al-Qamar said: 'With respect to Allah etc. Here, Bayan is only relative to servants. As for Allah, all things are apparent and known to Him, so it is not appropriate that Naskh be counted among the divisions of Bayan. Rather, it is the removal of the ruling after its establishment. That is why Shams al-A'imma did not make Naskh a division of Bayan.'
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage defines 'Bayan al-Tabdeel' (clarification through substitution), which is synonymous with Naskh (abrogation) in the Hanafi usul tradition. The author argues that Naskh is a form of Bayan (clarification) when viewed from the divine perspective: Allah always knew the temporal limit of the ruling, and the abrogating verse merely reveals that hidden limit. From the human perspective, however, it appears as a change (tabdeel) because the earlier ruling seemed indefinite. The example of the permissibility of wine illustrates this: it was initially permitted indefinitely in human understanding, then prohibited. For Allah, the prohibition clarified the actual timeframe, while for humans it was a substitution. The passage also includes linguistic and technical definitions of Naskh, citing Quranic verses (16:101 and 2:106) and noting that the term 'naskh' in language can mean removal or transfer. The commentator Al-Qamar critiques the inclusion of Naskh as a division of Bayan, noting that Shams al-A'imma excluded it because Bayan pertains to clarifying what is hidden to servants, whereas to Allah nothing is hidden. Thus Naskh is simply the removal of a ruling after its establishment.

Key Terms
بيان تبديل (bayan al-tabdeel): Abrogation (naskh) considered as a form of clarification when viewed from the perspective of divine knowledge, and substitution from the human perspective.
نسخ (naskh): The Lawgiver's removal of a legal ruling by a later legal evidence. Linguistically, shared between removal and transfer.
حكم مطلق (hukm mutlaq): A legal ruling that is not explicitly restricted by a time limit, giving it an apparent indefinite duration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is naskh considered a 'bayan' (clarification) from Allah's perspective?
A) Because Allah reveals a new ruling that was never known before
B) Because the abrogated ruling was always temporary in Allah's knowledge, and the abrogation reveals that temporal limit
C) Because human beings need clarification of all rulings
D) Because naskh removes a ruling permanently

Key Takeaway
Naskh is both bayan and tabdeel: it clarifies Allah's pre-eternal timeframe while appearing as a substitution to us.

Naskh — Abrogation

Definition and Conditions of Naskh (Abrogation)
Defining naskh, its subject, and conditions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define naskh, identify its mahall (subject), state its conditions, and explain why temporal limitation (taqit) and eternal duration (ta'bid) preclude abrogation.

Core Idea
Naskh applies only to changeable practical rulings; eternal or essential matters are beyond its scope.

In this passage, the author presents a detailed Hanafi analysis of naskh (abrogation), clarifying what kinds of rulings can be abrogated and what conditions must be met. He distinguishes between practical rulings (ahkam amaliyya) and creedal matters (i'tiqadiyyat), and then discusses two key preventers: temporal limitation (taqit) and eternal duration (ta'bid). The section also addresses a cross-madhhab dispute regarding the possibility of abrogating an eternally restricted ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central definition of naskh
Find the implied definition: 'رفع الحكم الشرعي بدليل شرعي متأخر' (removal of a legal ruling by a later legal evidence). Note that naskh is not arbitrary but requires a later revelation.
The definition is not stated verbatim but is the classical Hanafi understanding.
2
Locate the 'mahall' (subject) of naskh
The text states: 'ومحله حكم يحتمل الوجود والعدم في نفسه'. The subject is a ruling that in itself admits existence and non-existence. This means the ruling is contingent, not essential.
Essential beliefs like iman (faith) are necessary (wajib li-dhatihi) and thus cannot be abrogated.
3
List the conditions for a ruling to be abrogated
The ruling must be practical (عمليا), not necessary in itself (not like obligation of faith), nor impossible in itself (not like prohibition of disbelief). In other words, it must be a possible legal ruling that can vary.
Rational rulings (ahkam aqliyya) like knowledge of God's oneness are not subject to naskh.
4
Examine the preventers: taqit and ta'bid
Temporal limitation (توقيت): a ruling specified to a time cannot be abrogated before that time; after it, the ruling ends naturally, not by naskh. Eternal duration (تأبيد): if a ruling is explicitly or implicitly stated to last forever (e.g., 'abiding forever'), it cannot be abrogated because eternity contradicts the concept of removal.
The example from the Quran: 'فَاعْفُوا وَاصْفَحُوا حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ اللَّهُ بِأَمْرِهِ' (2:109) shows a temporally limited ruling.
5
Analyze the dispute on ta'bid
Some scholars (opposing school) argue that an eternally restricted ruling can be abrogated because absolute prohibition implies eternity yet is abrogable. The Hanafi response (al-Bazdawi) holds that explicit eternity (نصًا) or implicit (دلالة) establishes contradiction: ta'bid means the ruling is meant to last forever, so abrogation would negate its purpose.
The dispute has practical effect: for example, the eternity of paradise and hell for believers and disbelievers is non-abrogable according to Hanafis.

فصل في أقسام البيان ثم غدًا بخلاف ذلك، فإنه لا يحكم بسفاهته، بل هو عاقل حاذق يعطي كل يوم على ما يجد مزاجه فيه، و لم يقل من المريض: إني أبدلّك غذاءً بغذاء أو دواء آخر، وقد صح أن في شريعة آدم عليا كان نكاح الجزء أعني حوّاء حلالاً، وكذا نكاح الأخوات للأخ حلالاً، ثم نسخ في شريعة نوح علينا. ومحله حكم يحتمل الوجود والعدم في نفسه فعلم أن النسخ صحيح بأن يكون أمرًا ممكنا عمليًا ولا يكون واجبًا لذاته كالإيمان، ولا ممتنعا لذاته كالكفر، فإن وجوب الإيمان وحرمة الكفر لا ينسخ في دين من الأديان، ولا يقبل النسخ، ولم يلتحق به ما ينافي النسخ من توقيت عطف على قوله: "يحتمل الوجود"، لأنه إذا التحق به التوقيت لا ينسخ قبل ذلك الوقت ألبتة، وبعده لا يُطلق عليه اسم النسخ، وقد قالوا في نظيره: تَمَتَّعُوا فِي دَارِكُمْ ثَلاثَةَ أَيَّام خطاباً لقوم صالح عليه، وتَزْرَعُونَ سَبْعَ سنينَ دَأَبا حكايةً عن قول يوسف عليه كل ذلك غلط، لأنه من الأخبار والقصص، والأولى في نظيره قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْفُوا وَاصْفَحُوا حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ اللَّهُ بِأَمْرِهِ﴾ (البقرة : ١٠٩ ) وقد صح أن إلخ أي عندنا وعند اليهود أيضًا، فهذا دليل دال على وقوع النسخ، والغرض منه إلزام الخصم.(القمر) وقد صح إلخ روى الطبراني عن ابن مسعود وابن عباس لما كان لا يولد لآدم غلام إلا ولدت معه جارية، فكان يزوّج توأمة هذا للآخر، وتوأمة الآخر لهذا (السنبلي) ومحله أي محل النسخ بمعنى المنسوخية حكم شرعي يكون ثابتا بتعلّق الخطاب القديم الإلهي بأفعالنا اقتضاء أو تخييرًا أو وضعا، ويحتمل إلخ. (القمر) يحتمل الوجود إلخ إذ لو لم يحتمل الوجود أي الشرعية كالكفر يستمر عدمه أو العدم كإسلام يستمر وجوده ولا نسخ فيهما (السنبلي) عمليا أي لا عقليًا فإن الحكم العقلي لا يحتمل النسخ كإيمان وحدانيته تعالى (القمر) واجبًا لذاته أي حسنًا لذاته لا يحتمل عدم المشروعية . (القمر) ولا ممتنعا لذاته قبيحا لذاته لا يحتمل المشروعية . (القمر) ولم يلتحق به أي بذلك الحكم الذي ورد عليه النسخ. (القمر) لأنه من الأخبار إلخ وكلامنا في الأحكام الشرعية. (القمر) والأولى في نظيره إلخ: أي نظير الحكم المؤقت، وما في شرح المصنف تبعا لما نقل في "الكشف" من أنه ليس للحكم المؤقت مثال في "المنصوصات" كما نقله في مسير" : الدائر" فمن قلة التتبع (القمر) فاعفوا أي عن الكفار، واصفحوا أي أعرضوا.(القمر) وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ فِي الْبُيُوتِ حَتَّى يَتَوَفَّاهُنَّ الْمَوْتُ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ لَهُنَّ سَبِيلا﴾ (النساء : ١٥) ونحوه. أو تأبيد ثبت نصًا أو دلالة عطف على قوله: "توقيت" فإنه إذا لحقه تأبيد ثبت نصا بأن أي صراحة يذكر فيه صريحا لفظ "الأبد" أو "دلالة" كالشرائع التي قُبض عليها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يقبل النسخ؛ لأن التأبيد الصريح ينافي النسخ، وكذا لا نبي بعد نبينا، فلا ينسخ ما قبض عليه هو علية، وقد ذكروا في نظير التأييد الصريح قوله تعالى في حق الفريقين: خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا أي المؤمنين والكافرين في الجنة أو في جهنم أبدا، وأورد عليه بأنه يمكن أن يراد به المكث الطويل، وأجيب بأن ذلك فيما إذا اكتفي فأمسكوهن : أي الزوجات الزانيات بعد الإشهاد عليهن بالزنا في البيوت، ويُمنعن من مخالطة الناس حَتَّى يَتَوَفَّاهُنَّ الْمَوْتُ (النساء : ١٥) أي ملائكته أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللهُ لَهُنَّ سَبِيلاً (النساء : ١٥) طريقا إلى الخروج منها، وهذا في أول الإسلام ثم جعل الله لهن سبيلا بإنزال الحد. (القمر) أو تأبيد : أي دوام الحكم ما دام الدنيا. (القمر) التي قبض إلخ فإنها مؤبدة لا تقبل النسخ بدليل أنه لا نبي بعد نبينا ، والنسخ لا يكون إلا بالوحي على كذا قيل، ثم هذا عند من لم يجعل الإنساء نسخا بدليل أن عطف قوله تعالى : وننسها (البقرة: ١٠٦) على قوله تعالى: ننسخ (البقرة : ١٠٦) يدلّ على المغائرة، وأما عند من جعل الإنساء نسخا أيضًا بدليل أنهم أوردوا في كتبهم نظير نسخ التلاوة والحكم ما رفع من القرآن بالإنساء كما روي أن سورة الأحزاب كانت تعدل سورة البقرة، فرفع بالإنساء فيجوز نسخ تلك الشرائع بالإنساء وإن لم ينزل الوحي، لكنه لا يضرنا ههنا فإن النسخ بالإنساء إنما يمكن في حياة الرسول ، وأما بعد وفاته فهو ممتنع وإلا لزم الفتور وبطلان الشريعة، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَافِظُونَ﴾ (الحجر:۹) فتأمل. (القمر) ينافي النسخ إلخ: هذا هو مختار البزدوي، وقال بعضهم: إن نسخ الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد جائز فإن النسخ رفع حكم المنسوخ، فيجوز أن يرتفع الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد يمحو الله ما يشاء ويثبت ألا ترى أن النهي المطلق يدل على استيعاب الزمان والتأبيد مع أن نسخه جائز، فكذا الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد، ولا تناقض فإن الحكم الناسخ إنشاء، والحكم المنسوخ أيضًا إنشاء، فأحدهما صار رافعًا للآخر، وتابعوا فخر الإسلام البزدوي، ويقولون: إن قيد التأبيد لتأكيد الأحكام ولرفع احتمال النسخ فكيف يقبل النسخ؟ وقال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي بحاله: إنهم مؤاخذون بالدليل على ما قالوا، تأمل . (القمر) وقد ذكروا إلخ قلت وأيضًا قد ذكر بعضهم في مثاله قوله تعالى: ﴿وَجَاعِلُ الَّذِينَ اتَّبَعُوكَ فَوْقَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ (آل عمران: ٥٥) قوله علي: "الجهاد ماض إلى يوم القيامة" ووجه منافاة التأبيد للنسخ ظاهر ، وهو التناقض بينهما فإن التأبيد يقتضي بقاء الحكم أبدا، والنسخ ينافيه فإنه مقتضي الارتفاع، ومثل سائر شرائع محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم التي قبض على إقرارها فإنها مؤبدة لا يحتمل النسخ بدلالة أن محمدا لله خاتم النبيين ولا نبي بعده، ولا نسخ إلا بوحي على لسان نبي. (السنبلي)
Chapter on the divisions of al-bayan. Then tomorrow opposite to that, for he is not judged as foolish, rather he is an intelligent clever man who gives each day according to what he finds his temperament in it, and he did not say to the patient: I will change for you food for food or another medicine. And it is established that in the shariah of Adam (peace be upon him) the marriage of the part, meaning Eve, was permissible, and likewise the marriage of sisters to a brother was permissible, then it was abrogated in the shariah of Noah (peace be upon us). And its place [i.e., the subject of abrogation] is a ruling that in itself admits existence and non-existence. So it is known that abrogation is valid [only] if it is a practically possible matter, and it should not be necessary in itself like belief, nor impossible in itself like disbelief, for the obligation of belief and the prohibition of disbelief are not abrogated in any religion, and they do not accept abrogation. And what contradicts abrogation of temporal limitation is attached to it, as a continuation of his statement: 'admits existence', because if temporal limitation is attached to it, it is not abrogated before that time at all, and after it the name of abrogation is not applied to it. And they said about its analogue: 'Enjoy yourselves in your abode for three days' as an address to the people of Salih, and 'You will sow for seven consecutive years' as a narration from Yusuf's statement. All of that is wrong, because it is from reports and stories. The best in its analogue is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'So forgive and pardon until Allah brings His command.' (al-Baqarah: 109). And it is established that... etc., meaning according to us and also according to the Jews, so this is a proof indicating the occurrence of abrogation, and the purpose of it is to refute the opponent. (al-Qamar) 'And it is established that...' etc. al-Tabarani narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas: when no son was born to Adam except that a girl was born with him, so he would marry the twin of this one to the other, and the twin of the other to this one. (al-Sanbali) 'And its place' meaning the place of abrogation in the sense of being abrogated is a legal ruling established by the attachment of the eternal divine address to our actions, whether as a requirement, an option, or a constitutive ruling, and it admits... etc. (al-Qamar) 'admits existence' etc., for if it did not admit existence, i.e., legal existence, like disbelief, its non-existence continues, or non-existence, like Islam, its existence continues, and there is no abrogation in either. (al-Sanbali) 'Practical' meaning not rational, for rational rulings do not admit abrogation, like belief in His oneness. (al-Qamar) 'necessary in itself' meaning good in itself, does not admit absence of legality. (al-Qamar) 'nor impossible in itself' meaning evil in itself, does not admit legality. (al-Qamar) 'And what contradicts abrogation is attached to it' i.e., to that ruling which has undergone abrogation. (al-Qamar) 'because it is from reports' etc., and our discourse is about legal rulings. (al-Qamar) 'The best in its analogue' etc., i.e., the analogue of a temporally limited ruling. And what is in the commentary of the author following what is transmitted in al-Kashf that there is no example of a temporally limited ruling in the explicit texts, as transmitted in al-Masir: al-Da'ir, that is due to lack of research. (al-Qamar) 'So forgive' i.e., the disbelievers, 'and pardon' i.e., turn away. (al-Qamar) And His saying the Exalted: 'So confine them in houses until death takes them or Allah makes for them a way.' (al-Nisa: 15) and similar. Or eternal duration established by text or implication, as a continuation of his statement: 'temporal limitation' because if eternal duration attaches to it, established by text, i.e., explicitly mentioning the word 'eternity', or 'implication' like the laws upon which the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم passed away do not accept abrogation; because explicit eternity contradicts abrogation, and likewise there is no prophet after our Prophet, so what he passed away upon is not abrogated. And they mentioned concerning the analogue of explicit eternity His saying the Exalted regarding the two groups: 'abiding therein forever' i.e., the believers and disbelievers in Paradise or in Hell eternally. And it was objected that it could mean prolonged stay, and it was answered that that is when it is limited. So confine them: i.e., the adulterous wives after testifying against them of adultery in houses, and they are prevented from mixing with people until death takes them (al-Nisa: 15) i.e., His angels, 'or Allah makes for them a way' (al-Nisa: 15) a way to exit from them. And this was in early Islam, then Allah made for them a way by prescribing the legal punishment. (al-Qamar) 'Or eternal duration' i.e., the continuation of the ruling as long as the world lasts. (al-Qamar) 'those laws upon which...' etc., they are eternal, do not accept abrogation, evidenced that there is no prophet after our Prophet, and abrogation only occurs through revelation. So it is said, then this is according to those who do not consider insa' (causing forgetfulness) as abrogation, evidenced that the conjunction of His saying: 'and cause to forget' (al-Baqarah: 106) to His saying: 'We abrogate' (al-Baqarah: 106) indicates difference. And as for those who consider insa' also as abrogation, evidenced that they mentioned in their books the analogue of abrogation of recitation and ruling, that which was removed from the Quran by insa', as it is narrated that Surat al-Ahzab used to equal Surat al-Baqarah, then it was removed by insa', so it is permissible to abrogate those laws by insa' even if revelation was not sent down. But that does not harm us here, for abrogation by insa' is only possible during the lifetime of the Messenger, while after his death it is impossible, otherwise it would lead to discontinuity and invalidation of the shariah. And Allah the Exalted said: 'Indeed, We have sent down the Reminder, and indeed, We will be its guardian.' (al-Hijr: 9) So reflect. (al-Qamar) 'contradicts abrogation' etc.: this is the choice of al-Bazdawi. And some said: abrogation of a ruling restricted by eternity is permissible, for abrogation is the removal of the abrogated ruling, so it is permissible that the ruling restricted by eternity be removed. 'Allah erases what He wills and establishes.' Do you not see that absolute prohibition indicates continuity of time and eternity, yet its abrogation is permissible? So likewise the ruling restricted by eternity. There is no contradiction, for the abrogating ruling is a new legislation, and the abrogated ruling is also a legislation, so one of them becomes a remover of the other. They followed Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, and they say: the restriction of eternity is for emphasis of rulings and to remove the possibility of abrogation, so how can it accept abrogation? And Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana 'Abd al-Al said: they are bound by the evidence on what they said. Reflect. (al-Qamar) 'And they mentioned' etc. I say: also some mentioned as its example His saying the Exalted: 'And those who follow you I will place above those who disbelieve until the Day of Resurrection.' (Al 'Imran: 55) and his saying عليه: 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection.' The aspect of the conflict between eternity and abrogation is apparent: it is the contradiction between them, for eternity requires the persistence of the ruling forever, and abrogation contradicts it, for it requires removal. And like the rest of the shariahs of Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم which he passed away confirming them, they are eternal, do not admit abrogation, evidenced that Muhammad صلى الله عليه وسلم is the seal of the prophets, and there is no prophet after him, and abrogation only occurs through revelation on the tongue of a prophet. (al-Sanbali)
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul discussion on the nature and conditions of naskh (abrogation). It begins by defining the subject (mahall) of naskh: it must be a ruling that is capable of both existence and non-existence. This excludes essential beliefs like iman (faith) and kufr (disbelief), which are necessary or impossible in themselves and thus not subject to abrogation. The author also clarifies that naskh applies only to practical (amali) rulings, not rational (aqli) ones. The discussion then addresses two factors that preclude naskh: temporal limitation (taqit) and eternal duration (ta'bid). A temporally limited ruling cannot be abrogated before its term, and after its term it is not called naskh. An eternally binding ruling (like those confirmed by the Prophet's death or explicit mention of 'forever') also cannot be abrogated, as eternity and abrogation are contradictory. The text provides examples from earlier scriptures (marriage of twins in Adam's shariah abrogated in Noah's) and from the Quran (the verse 'forgive until Allah brings His command' is given as a correct example of a temporally limited ruling, unlike the stories of Salih and Yusuf which are narratives, not legal rulings). The commentary (from al-Qamar and al-Sanbali) further elaborates on the definition, citing al-Bazdawi's position and addressing objections. There is a notable dispute: some scholars allow abrogation of eternally restricted rulings, arguing that absolute prohibition implies eternity yet is abrogable. However, the Hanafi position (as per al-Bazdawi) maintains that explicit eternity (ta'bid) prevents naskh because it would be contradictory. The passage also touches on the concept of insa' (causing forgetfulness) as a form of abrogation only possible during the Prophet's lifetime, not after. After the Prophet's death, no abrogation can occur because there is no further revelation. This understanding is anchored in Quran 15:9 ('We have sent down the Reminder, and indeed We will be its guardian'). The overall lesson is that naskh is a well-defined concept with strict conditions, and it does not apply to fundamental beliefs or eternally established rulings.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): رفع الحكم الشرعي بدليل شرعي متأخر
توقيت (taqit): تحديد الحكم بزمن معين فلا ينسخ قبله ولا بعد
تأبيد (ta'bid): دوام الحكم أبدا بصيغة صريحة أو دلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basic condition for a legal ruling to be subject to naskh according to the Hanafi school in this passage?
A) It must be a rational necessary truth.
B) It must be a practical ruling that in itself admits existence and non-existence.
C) It must be explicitly stated to last forever.
D) It must be a narrative from earlier scriptures.

Key Takeaway
Naskh in Hanafi usul is strictly limited to practical rulings that are neither temporally fixed nor eternally binding.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
8 min
The Non-Abrogability of Perpetual Rulings (Mu'abbad): Al-Bazdawi's View
Dispute over whether perpetual (mu'abbad) rulings can be abrogated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school (following al-Bazdawi) holds that a ruling explicitly designated as perpetual (mu'abbad) cannot be abrogated, and evaluate the opposing argument.

Core Idea
Explicit perpetuity and abrogation are logically contradictory: one requires forever, the other removal.

Abrogation (naskh) is a key concept in usul al-fiqh, but not all rulings are subject to it. This passage from Noor al-Anwar examines a dispute within the Hanafi school: can a ruling that is explicitly called 'perpetual' (mu'abbad) ever be abrogated? Al-Bazdawi argues it cannot, while some scholars disagree. Understanding this dispute sheds light on how the Hanafi school safeguards the finality of Prophethood and the integrity of the Shariah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ta'bīd
The author defines ta'bīd as either explicit (nas) through the word 'abdan' or indicative (dalala) like the laws the Prophet passed away upon.
Explicit perpetuity is stronger than indicative.
2
State al-Bazdawi's position and key proof
Al-Bazdawi argues that explicit perpetuity contradicts abrogation. His main proof: 'No prophet after me' so no new revelation can abrogate.
This relies on the khatamiyyah (finality) of Prophethood.
3
Examine the opposing argument and its basis
Opponents say absolute prohibitions imply perpetuity yet are abrogated, so explicit perpetuity can also be abrogated by new legislation.
They view abrogation as mere replacement, not contradiction.
4
Understand the distinction between akhbār and ahkām
The passage clarifies that some perpetual statements are reports (akhbar) that cannot be abrogated without changing truth value, while others are rulings (ahkam).
Reports like 'khālidīna fīhā' are not abrogable because they inform about a reality.
5
Apply the principle to a key example
The verse 'wa lā taqbalū lahum shahādatan abadā' (24:4) is a perpetual report-ruling and thus non-abrogable.
This example is specifically approved by the author.

بیان تبدیل
وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ فِي الْبُيُوتِ حَتَّى يَتَوَفَّاهُنَّ الْمَوْتُ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ لَهُنَّ سَبِيلا ونحوه. (النساء : ١٥) أو تأبيد ثبت نصًا أو دلالة عطف على قوله: "توقيت" فإنه إذا لحقه تأبيد ثبت نصا بأن أي صراحة يذكر فيه صريحا لفظ "الأبد" أو "دلالة" كالشرائع التي قُبض عليها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يقبل النسخ؛ لأن التأبيد الصريح ينافي النسخ، وكذا لا نبي بعد نبينا، فلا ينسخ ما قبض عليه هو علية، وقد ذكروا في نظير التأييد الصريح قوله تعالى في حق الفريقين: خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا أي المؤمنين والكافرين في الجنة أو في جهنم أبدا، وأورد عليه بأنه يمكن أن يراد به المكث الطويل، وأجيب بأن ذلك فيما إذا اكتفي (النساء: ٥٧) فأمسكوهن : أي الزوجات الزانيات بعد الإشهاد عليهن بالزنا في البيوت، ويُمنعن من مخالطة الناس حَتَّى يَتَوَفَّاهُنَّ الْمَوْتُ (النساء : ١٥) أي ملائكته أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللهُ لَهُنَّ سَبِيلاً (النساء : ١٥) طريقا إلى الخروج منها، وهذا في طالله أول الإسلام ثم جعل الله لهن سبيلا بإنزال الحد. (القمر) أو تأبيد : أي دوام الحكم ما دام الدنيا. (القمر) التي قبض إلخ فإنها مؤبدة لا تقبل النسخ بدليل أنه لا نبي بعد نبينا ، والنسخ لا يكون إلا بالوحي على كذا قيل، ثم هذا عند من لم يجعل الإنساء نسخا بدليل أن عطف قوله تعالى : وننسها (البقرة: ١٠٦) على قوله تعالى: ننسخ (البقرة : ١٠٦) يدلّ على المغائرة، وأما عند من جعل الإنساء نسخا أيضًا بدليل أنهم أوردوا في كتبهم نظير نسخ التلاوة والحكم ما رفع من القرآن بالإنساء كما روي أن سورة الأحزاب كانت تعدل سورة البقرة، فرفع بالإنساء فيجوز نسخ تلك الشرائع بالإنساء وإن لم ينزل الوحي، لكنه لا يضرنا ههنا فإن النسخ بالإنساء إنما يمكن في حياة الرسول ، وأما بعد وفاته فهو ممتنع وإلا لزم الفتور وبطلان الشريعة، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَافِظُونَ) (الحجر:۹) فتأمل. (القمر) ينافي النسخ إلخ: هذا هو مختار البزدوي، وقال بعضهم: إن نسخ الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد جائز فإن النسخ رفع حكم المنسوخ، فيجوز أن يرتفع الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد يمحو الله ما يشاء ويثبت ألا ترى أن النهي المطلق يدل على استيعاب الزمان والتأبيد مع أن نسخه جائز، فكذا الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد، ولا تناقض فإن الحكم الناسخ إنشاء، والحكم المنسوخ أيضًا إنشاء، فأحدهما صار رافعًا للآخر، وتابعوا فخر الإسلام البزدوي، ويقولون: إن قيد التأبيد لتأكيد الأحكام ولرفع احتمال النسخ فكيف يقبل النسخ؟ وقال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي بحاله: إنهم مؤاخذون بالدليل على ما قالوا، تأمل . (القمر) وقد ذكروا إلخ قلت وأيضًا قد ذكر بعضهم في مثاله قوله تعالى: ﴿وَجَاعِلُ الَّذِينَ اتَّبَعُوكَ فَوْقَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ (آل عمران: ٥٥) قوله علي: "الجهاد ماض إلى يوم القيامة" ووجه منافاة التأبيد للنسخ ظاهر ، وهو التناقض بينهما فإن التأبيد يقتضي بقاء الحكم أبدا، والنسخ ينافيه فإنه مقتضي الارتفاع، ومثل سائر شرائع محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم التي قبض على إقرارها فإنها مؤبدة لا يحتمل النسخ بدلالة أن محمدا لله خاتم النبيين ولا نبي بعده، ولا نسخ إلا بوحي على لسان نبي. (السنبلي) فصل في أقسام البيان بيان تبدیل بقوله: "خالدين" كما في حق العُصاة، وأما إذا قرن بقوله : "أبدًا" فإنه صار محكما في التأبيد الحقيقي، والكل غلط؛ لأنه في الأخبار دون الأحكام والأولى في نظيره قوله تعالى في المحدود في القذف: ﴿وَلا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبدا فإنه لا ينسخ. (النور: ٤)
Chapter on the divisions of Bayan. Bayan Tabdil. And His saying Exalted: 'So confine them in their homes until death takes them or Allah makes for them a way' etc. Or perpetual (ta'bid) established by explicit text or indication, conjoined to his saying: 'temporal restriction'. For if a perpetual restriction attaches to it, it is established by explicit text meaning explicitly mentioning the word 'eternity' or by indication like the laws upon which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) passed away are not subject to abrogation; because explicit perpetuity contradicts abrogation, and likewise there is no prophet after our Prophet, so what he passed away upon cannot be abrogated. And they mentioned as an example of explicit perpetuity His Exalted saying regarding the two groups: 'abiding eternally therein' meaning the believers and disbelievers in Paradise or Hell forever. And objection was raised that it could mean prolonged stay. And it was answered that that applies when content with... 'Confine them' meaning the adulterous wives after testifying against them for adultery in their homes, prevented from mixing with people until death takes them or Allah makes for them a way. This was at the beginning of Islam, then Allah made for them a way by revealing the [prescribed] punishment. (al-Qamar) Or perpetuity: meaning continuation of the ruling for the duration of this world. (al-Qamar) Those upon which he passed away etc. are perpetual, not subject to abrogation, evidenced by the fact that there is no prophet after our Prophet, and abrogation is only by revelation. This is according to those who do not consider insa' (causing to forget) as abrogation, evidenced by the conjunction of His saying 'and We cause to forget' upon 'We abrogate' indicating difference. As for those who consider insa' as abrogation also, evidenced by that they cited in their books as similar to abrogation of recitation and ruling what was raised from the Quran by insa' as reported that Surah al-Ahzab was equal to Surah al-Baqarah and was raised by insa'. So it is permissible to abrogate those laws by insa' even if no revelation descended. But that does not harm us here, for abrogation by insa' only possible during the Prophet's lifetime, after his death it is impossible otherwise it would entail annulment and invalidation of the shariah. And Allah said: 'Indeed, We have sent down the Reminder and indeed We are its Preserver' (15:9) so ponder. (al-Qamar) It contradicts abrogation etc.: This is the choice of al-Bazdawi. And some said: abrogation of a ruling qualified by perpetuity is permissible, because abrogation is removal of the abrogated ruling, so it is permissible for the ruling qualified by perpetuity to be removed; Allah effaces what He wills and establishes. Do you not see that absolute prohibition indicates encompassment of time and perpetuity, yet its abrogation is permissible? So too a ruling qualified by perpetuity. And there is no contradiction, for the abrogating ruling is new legislation and the abrogated ruling is also new legislation, so one becomes a remover of the other. And they followed Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, and they say: The qualification of perpetuity is to emphasize rulings and to remove the possibility of abrogation, so how can it accept abrogation? And Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali said in his condition: They are answerable based on evidence for what they said, ponder. (al-Qamar) And they mentioned etc. I say: Also some have mentioned as an example His saying: 'And [He] will make those who follow you superior to those who disbelieve until the Day of Resurrection' (3:55), and his saying (Ali): 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection'. And the manner of contradiction between perpetuity and abrogation is apparent, which is the contradiction between them: perpetuity requires the survival of the ruling forever, and abrogation contradicts it for it necessitates removal. And like the other laws of Muhammad (peace be upon him) which he passed away affirming, they are perpetual, not susceptible to abrogation, evidenced by the fact that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets and no prophet after him, and there is no abrogation except by revelation upon the tongue of a prophet. (al-Sanbali) Chapter on the divisions of Bayan. Bayan Tabdil. By His saying 'eternally' as in the case of the disobedient, but if conjoined with His saying 'forever' then it becomes decisive in the true perpetuity. And all of this is wrong, because it pertains to reports, not rulings. And the appropriate example is His saying regarding the one flogged for slander: 'And do not accept from them any testimony forever' (24:4) which cannot be abrogated.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) within Hanafi usul regarding whether a ruling explicitly qualified as perpetual (mu'abbad) can be abrogated (naskh). The author begins by defining two types of perpetual establishment: explicit (nas) such as the word 'abdan' (forever), and indicative (dalala) like the laws upon which the Prophet passed away. He then presents the position of al-Bazdawi that explicit perpetuity precludes abrogation because it would contradict the very wording. They cite verses like 'abiding eternally therein' (khālidīna fīhā) as examples of perpetual statements. However, an objection is raised that such verses might mean prolonged stay, not true eternity. The response distinguishes between reports (akhbār) and rulings (ahkām): perpetual statements in reports (like eternal punishment) are not abrogable because they are truthful reports, whereas rulings are different. The opposing view argues that even a perpetual ruling can be abrogated because abrogation is simply removing one ruling by another, and the absolute prohibition (which implies perpetuity) can indeed be abrogated. The author follows al-Bazdawi, concluding that perpetual rulings concerning laws that the Prophet left upon are not abrogable, as there is no prophet after him to bring new revelation. The passage ends by refining the example: the verse about refusing testimony of slanderers forever is a better example of a perpetual ruling that cannot be abrogated because it is a report (khabar) about a ruling, not a ruling itself. The lesson emphasizes the Hanafi position that perpetuity (ta'bīd) is a strong indicator of non-abrogability, especially for laws established after the finality of prophethood.

Key Terms
تأبيد (ta'bīd): The quality of a ruling being perpetual or everlasting, either explicitly stated or indicated.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later divine revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does al-Bazdawi argue that the laws upon which the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) passed away cannot be abrogated?
A) Because they are recorded in the Quran.
B) Because there is no prophet after him to bring new revelation.
C) Because they are all about acts of worship.
D) Because they are supported by ijma.

Key Takeaway
Explicit perpetuity (ta'bīd) in a ruling makes it non-abrogable because perpetuity and abrogation are mutually exclusive, especially given the finality of Prophethood.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
8 min
Condition for Abrogation: Ability to Believe vs Ability to Act
Condition for naskh: mental acknowledgment sufficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition for naskh (ability to believe) and contrast it with the Mu'tazilite requirement of ability to act, citing the Mi'raj proof.

Core Idea
For naskh to be valid, the mukallaf need only have a moment to mentally affirm the command — not to perform it.

This lesson explores a foundational Hanafi usul principle: what must be possible for a revealed command to be abrogated? The Hanafi school holds that only the ability to mentally acknowledge (tamakkun min 'aqd al-qalb) is needed, while the Mu'tazila (and some Shafi'is and Hanbalis) insist on a period sufficient for physical action. The proof is the famous Mi'raj incident of fifty prayers abrogated to five before any performance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi rule
Identify the exact condition: 'tamakkun min 'aqd al-qalb' (ability to believe) is sufficient; 'tamakkun min al-fi'l' (ability to act) is not required.
This is the core usul rule for naskh in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view
The Mu'tazila and some followers of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad ibn Hanbal require a period where the commanded act can be physically performed before naskh is valid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in usul.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof (Mi'raj)
The Prophet was commanded with fifty daily prayers on Mi'raj, then abrogated to five within the same night. No one had time to pray fifty, but the Prophet believed the command instantly. His belief suffices for the entire community as he is their imam.
The abrogation occurred before descending to earth, emphasizing the immediacy.
4
Address the potential objection
Objection: The community was not informed, so how could they believe? Response: The command was initially on the Prophet; his belief stood for the whole ummah due to his role as leader.
This defends the validity of the naskh for the entire community.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a ruling is revealed and abrogated before anyone acts on it, Hanafis accept the naskh; Mu'tazila reject it as invalid because no action was possible.
This shows the real-world impact of the usul difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرطه التمكن من عقد القلب عندنا دون التمكن من الفعل، يعني لا بد بعد وصول الأمر إلى المكلّف من زمان قليل يتمكن فيه من اعتقاد ذلك الأمر حتى يقبل النسخ بعده، ولا يشترط فيه فصل زمان يتمكّن فيه من فعل ذلك الأمر خلافًا للمعتزلة، فإن عندهم لا بد من زمان التمكن من الفعل حتى يقبل النسخ ولنا: أن النبي عليه أمر بخمسين صلاةً في ليلة المعراج، ثم نسخ ما زاد على الخمس في ساعة* و لم يتمكن أحد من النبي أي في اليوم والليلة اعتقادها فقط، وإنه إمام الأمة، فيكفي والأمة من فعلها، وإنما يتمكن النبي من من اعتقادهم، فكأنهم اعتقدوها جميعًا، ثم نسخت. أي الأمة اعتقاده في التأبيد إلخ فلا يقبل النسخ ، تأمل (القمر) والكل أي التنظير والإيراد والجواب. (القمر) لأنه في الأخبار إلخ ونسخ الأخبار لا يجوز لأن الخبر لا بد في صدقه من تحقق المحكي عنه في زمانه مع قطع النظر عن الخبر، فبالنسخ لا يرتفع المحكى عن زمانه، فلا يتبدل الخبر، فلا يتحقق النسخ، فامتناع النسخ فيما ذكر لكونه خبرًا لا للتأبيد. (القمر) والأولى في نظيره أي نظير التأبيد الصريح، وما في شرح "الحسامي" من أنه لم يوجد في الأحكام تأبيد صريح انتهى فهو من قلة التتبع (القمر) ولا يشترط إلخ : أي لا يشترط أن يمضي بعد وصول الأمر إلى المكلّف زمان يسع الفعل المأمور به ويتمكّن من فعله في ذلك الزمان. (القمر) للمعتزلة ولبعض مشايخنا ولبعض أصحاب الشافعي محله ولبعض أصحاب أحمد بن حنبل له (القمر) د. في ساعة أي قبل النزول إلى الأرض. (القمر) وإنه إمام الأمة إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر، تقريره: أنا سلّمنا أن النبي تمكن اعتقادها، لكن الأمة ما كان لهم خبر بفرضية الخمسين، فلم يتمكنوا على اعتقادها، فلزم نسخ فرضية الخمسين عن الأمة قبل التمكن من اعتقادها، وهذا خلف.(القمر) من ثم نسخت وههنا شبهة وتقريرها أن قبل تبليغ النبي الله لا يصير شيء فرضًا على الأمة، والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ما بلغ الأمة فرضية خمسين صلاة، فكيف افترضت على الأمة حتى يقال: إنها نسخت قبل التمكن من الفعل؟ وإن قيل: مذكور في حديث طويل روي عن مالك بن صعصعة في الصحيحين وغيرهما. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٥]
And its condition [i.e., condition for naskh] according to us is the ability of the heart's conviction (tamakkun min 'aqd al-qalb), not the ability to act. Meaning: after the command reaches the responsible person, a little time must pass in which he can believe that command, so that the naskh can occur afterwards. It is not required that a period separate in which he can perform that act, contrary to the Mu'tazila. According to them, a period of ability to act is necessary for naskh. And for us: The Prophet (peace be upon him) was commanded with fifty prayers on the night of the Mi'raj, then what exceeded five was abrogated within an hour, and no one was able to [perform] from the Prophet] in the day and night except belief in them only, and he is the leader of the community, so it suffices. And the community from their action, and the Prophet only [needed] their belief, as if they all believed them, then they were abrogated. i.e., the community's belief. In perpetuity etc. so it does not accept abrogation, ponder. (al-Qamar) And all, i.e., the classification, objection, and response. (al-Qamar) Because it is in reports etc. and abrogation of reports is impermissible because for a report's truthfulness, the reality of the reported matter in its time must be verified, irrespective of the report. So by abrogation, the reported matter does not cease from its time, so the report does not change, so naskh does not occur. So the prevention of naskh in what was mentioned is because it is a report, not because of perpetuity. (al-Qamar) And the more appropriate in its counterpart i.e., counterpart of explicit perpetuity, and what is in the commentary of al-Husami that there is no explicit perpetuity in rulings is due to lack of investigation. (al-Qamar) And it is not required etc.: meaning it is not required that after the command reaches the responsible person, a period passes that accommodates the commanded action and he can perform it within that period. (al-Qamar) For the Mu'tazila and some of our scholars and some of al-Shafi'i's followers and some of Ahmad ibn Hanbal's followers. (al-Qamar) In an hour: meaning before descending to earth. (al-Qamar) And he is the leader of the community etc.: to repulse a potential objection. Its summary: We concede that the Prophet could believe them, but the community had no knowledge of the obligation of fifty, so they could not believe them. Thus, the abrogation of the fifty from the community occurred before their ability to believe, and this is a counterexample. (al-Qamar) Then they were abrogated. And here is a doubt: Its presentation: That before the Prophet's conveying, nothing becomes obligatory on the community, and the Prophet did not convey to the community the obligation of fifty prayers, so how was it obligatory upon the community so that it is said it was abrogated before ability to act? And if it is said: It is mentioned in a long hadith narrated from Malik ibn Sa'sa'ah in the Sahihs and others. [Ishraq al-Absar 25]
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul rule (qā'ida) concerning the condition for abrogation (naskh). The rule states that for a command to be abrogated, the responsible person (mukallaf) must have had the ability to mentally acknowledge (i'tiqād) the command, not the ability to physically perform it. This is the Hanafi position, contrary to the Mu'tazila, who require actual ability to act (tamakkun min al-fi'l). The proof (dalīl) is the story of the fifty prayers during the Mi'raj: the Prophet was commanded with fifty daily prayers, and immediately (within the same night) it was abrogated to five. Neither the Prophet nor the community had time to perform fifty prayers, but the Prophet was able to believe the command, and his belief sufficed for the entire community because he is their imam. The passage then addresses a potential objection: How can the obligation be deemed to have been on the community when they were never informed? The answer (defence) is that the command was addressed to the Prophet first, and his belief represented the community's belief by virtue of his leadership. Thus, naskh can occur even before the command is conveyed to the community, as long as the Prophet (or the immediate addressee) had the opportunity to believe. The passage also includes marginal clarifications: the earlier discussion about perpetuity (ta'bīd) preventing naskh is actually because such texts are reports (akhbār), not because of perpetuity itself. And it criticizes al-Husami's claim that no explicit perpetuity exists in rulings, attributing it to lack of research. This lesson teaches that the essence of naskh is about legislative change, not physical implementation.

Key Terms
تمكن من عقد القلب (tamakkun min 'aqd al-qalb): The ability to mentally affirm and intend the command in one's heart.
التمكن من الفعل (al-tamakkun min al-fi'l): Possessing the capability and opportunity to physically perform the commanded act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the minimum requirement for a command to be validly abrogated?
A) The addressee must have performed the commanded act at least once.
B) The addressee must have had a moment to mentally affirm the command.
C) The command must have been conveyed to all future generations.
D) The abrogation must occur after the death of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Abrogation requires only a moment of mental acknowledgment, not physical performance.
