فصل في أقسام البيان بيان جواز النسخ بالكتاب. إلى بيت المقدس في وقت قدوم المدينة كان ثابتًا بالسنة بالاتفاق، ثم نسخ بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَوَل وَجْهَكَ شَطْرَ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ﴾، ونسخ الكتاب بالسنة مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿لا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ مِنْ بَعْدُ﴾ أي بعد التسع، نسخ بما روت عائشة لها أن النبي عليه أخبرها بأن الله تعالى أباح له من النساء ما شاء، وقيل: هو منسوخ بالآية التي قبلها في التلاوة، أعني قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَحْلَلْنَا لَكَ أَزْوَاجَكَ اللَّاتِي آتَيْتَ أُجُورَهُنَّ﴾ الآيةَ؛ (الأحزاب: ٥٠) كان ثابتا بالسنة إلخ فإنه علي كان يتوجه إلى الكعبة في الصلاة حين كان بمكة بناءً على ملة إبراهيم عليه، ثم تحوّل إلى بيت المقدس ستة عشر شهراً بالمدينة بالسنة إجماعًا لتألّف اليهود كذا قال العلي القاري بالله، وقال في "التلويح : فيه بحث؛ إذ لا دليل على كون التوجه إلى بيت المقدس ثابتا بالسنة سوى أنه غير متلو في القرآن، وهو يوجب التيقن بأنه من السنة. أقول وبالله التوفيق: إنه وإن كان لا يوجب التيقّن فلا أقل من الظن، وهو كافٍ للاحتجاج علا أن السنة قد ظهرت لنا والكتاب لم يظهر بل هو مجرد احتمال لا دليل عليه؛ فالحمل على السنة الظاهرة متعين. (القمر) فوَلِّ: أي اصرف وجهك واستقبل في الصلاة شطر نحو المسجد الحرام، أي الكعبة. (القمر) ونسخ الكتاب بالسنة إلخ : قال القاضي الإمام أبو زيد: لا يوجد في كتاب الله تعالى ما كان منسوخا بالسنة إلا بطريق الزيادة على النص. (القمر) بما روت عائشة لها إلخ كذا أورد العلي القارئ، وقال في يه، "التلويح : فيه بحث؛ لأن الكتاب لا ينسخ بخبر الواحد فكيف ينسخ ههنا بإخبار عائشة؟ وأشار الشيخ ابن اليسر إلى أن حرمة الزيادة على التسع حكم لا يحتمل النسخ؛ لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿مِنْ بَعْدِ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٧) بمنزلة التأبيد؛ إذ العبدية المطلقة تتناول الأبد، ويمكن أن يقال: إن الصحابي الذي روى هذا الخبر يعتقد وقوع نسخ الكتاب به، فإن هذا الخبر عنده ليس خبر الواحد، بل هو سمع من في رسول الله، فتجويز ذالك الصحابي النسخ بالخبر الذي رواه مما لا ينكر عليه؛ لأن الصحابة لهم عدول، بل يقبلونه؛ فلذا قلنا بوقوع نسخ الكتاب بالخبر تأمل.(القمر) وقيل هو : أي قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا يَحِلُّ لَكَ﴾ (الأحزاب: ٥٢) الآية. (القمر) وهو ما روى ابن جرير وغيره بسند جيد قوي عن ابن عباس قال : لما هاجر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى المدينة أمره الله أن يستقبل بيت المقدس. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٦] ** أخرجه عبد الرزاق والنسائي وأحمد والترمذي والحاكم وصححاه وغيرهم عنها قالت: لم يمت رسول الله حتى أحل الله له من النساء ما شاء أن يتزوجها إلا ذات محرم، وأخرج ابن أبي حاتم عن أم سلمة نحوه. [إشراق الأبصار: ٢٦]
Chapter on divisions of Bayan: Explanation of the permissibility of abrogation by the Book. To Jerusalem at the time of arrival in Medina was established by Sunnah by consensus, then it was abrogated by His saying, the Exalted: 'So turn your face toward al-Masjid al-Haram' (2:144). And abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah is like His saying, the Exalted: 'Women are not lawful for you after that' i.e., after nine, abrogated by what Aisha narrated that the Prophet informed her that Allah the Exalted permitted for him of women whatever he wished. And it is said: it is abrogated by the verse that precedes it in recitation, namely His saying, the Exalted: 'Indeed, We have made lawful for you your wives to whom you have given their bridal dues' (33:50). It was established by the Sunnah etc. For he used to face the Kaaba in prayer when he was in Mecca based on the religion of Ibrahim, then he turned to Jerusalem for sixteen months in Medina by the Sunnah by consensus to win over the Jews. Thus said al-‘Ali al-Qari. And he said in al-Talwih: There is discussion, for there is no evidence that facing Jerusalem was established by the Sunnah except that it is not recited in the Quran, which necessitates certainty that it is from the Sunnah. I say, and with Allah is success: Even if it does not necessitate certainty, it is at least a probability, and that is sufficient for argument; rather the Sunnah has appeared to us and the Book has not appeared, it is mere probability with no evidence; so relying on the apparent Sunnah is necessary. (Al-Qamar) 'Fa-walli': meaning turn your face and face in prayer toward al-Masjid al-Haram, i.e., the Kaaba. (Al-Qamar) And abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah etc. Al-Qadi Imam Abu Zayd said: There does not exist in the Book of Allah the Exalted anything that was abrogated by the Sunnah except by way of addition to the text. (Al-Qamar) By what Aisha narrated etc. Thus al-‘Ali al-Qari quoted, and he said in al-Talwih: There is discussion, because the Book cannot be abrogated by a khabar al-wahid; so how is it abrogated here by the report of Aisha? And Shaykh Ibn al-Yasir indicated that the prohibition of exceeding nine is a ruling that does not admit abrogation, because His saying 'after that' (2:27) is like eternalization, since absolute eternity encompasses the infinite. And it can be said: The Companion who reported this narration believed that abrogation of the Book occurred by it; for this report in his view is not a khabar al-wahid, but rather he heard it from the Messenger of Allah. So that Companion's deeming abrogation by the report he narrated is not criticized, because the Companions are upright; rather it is accepted. Hence we say that abrogation of the Book by the report occurred. (Al-Qamar) And it is said: i.e., His saying 'Women are not lawful for you' (33:52) the verse. (Al-Qamar) And that which Ibn Jarir and others narrated with a good strong chain from Ibn Abbas, he said: When the Messenger of Allah migrated to Medina, Allah commanded him to face Jerusalem. [Ishraq al-Absar 26] ** Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq, al-Nasa'i, Ahmad, al-Tirmidhi, al-Hakim, and they authenticated it and others, from her (Aisha), she said: The Messenger of Allah did not die until Allah made lawful for him from women whatever he wished to marry except a mahram. And Ibn Abi Hatim narrated from Umm Salamah similar to it. [Ishraq al-Absar: 26]
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn discussing the permissibility of abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah. The author presents two examples: first, the abrogation of facing Jerusalem in prayer (established by Sunnah) by the Quranic verse commanding facing the Kaaba; second, the verse limiting the Prophet's wives to nine abrogated by a hadith narrated by Aisha. The commentator then addresses objections: from al-Talwih questioning whether facing Jerusalem was proven by Sunnah, and from Abu Zayd limiting abrogation by Sunnah to additions. On the Aisha hadith, the commentator notes the debate over abrogation by khabar al-wahid, citing Ibn al-Yasir's argument that the verse is perpetual and the Companion's acceptance of the report as mutawatir. The passage ends with supporting narrations from Ibn Abbas and Aisha.

Key Terms
نسخ الكتاب بالسنة (naskh al-kitab bi al-sunnah): Abrogation of a Quranic ruling by a later Sunnah (hadith), whether mutawatir or ahad.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary hadith narrated by one or a few chains, lacking tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one objection raised against using the hadith of Aisha to abrogate the verse limiting the Prophet's marriage?
A) The hadith is contradictory to the Quran.
B) The Quran cannot be abrogated by khabar al-wahid.
C) The Prophet never married more than nine women.
D) The verse was already abrogated by another verse.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul allows abrogation of a Quranic ruling by an ahad hadith if the Companion narrator treated it as authoritative, reflecting a practical approach to evidence hierarchy.

Naskh — Abrogation

Types of Mansukh: Abrogation of Recitation and Ruling vs. Ruling Only
Classifying abrogated Quranic verses into two types based on whether the recitation and ruling are both abrogated or only the ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the two types of mansukh in the Quran, cite examples for each, and explain their implications for usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Abrogation can remove both the wording and ruling of a Quranic verse, or only the ruling while the wording remains.

In this lesson, we examine the classification of abrogated (mansukh) verses in the Quran. The author distinguishes between two types: those where both the recitation and the ruling are removed, and those where only the ruling is abrogated while the verse remains in the mushaf. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying naskh in legal deduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the Arabic text to identify the two types: 'mansukh al-tilawah wa al-hukm' and 'mansukh al-hukm duna al-tilawah'. Note the wording used.
The first type is also referred to as 'al-mansukh al-tilawah wa al-hukm'.
2
Understand the mechanism of the first type
The first type occurs by insa' (causing forgetfulness) during the Prophet's lifetime. The verse was removed from the Quranic text entirely.
This is specific to the time of revelation.
3
Analyze the examples
Surah al-Ahzab and Surah al-Talaq were originally much longer but now remain shorter; the extra part is abrogated in both recitation and ruling. Understand the evidence from companion reports.
The exact original length is based on reports, not qat'i.
4
Understand the second type
The second type keeps the recitation but the ruling is abrogated by a later verse. Example: verse 109:6 abrogated by verses of fighting.
This is common and widely accepted.
5
Recognize the scope
This classification is specifically for abrogation from the Book, not absolute naskh. The commentator restricts it to Quranic naskh.
The distinction helps in categorizing different types of naskh in the sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام البيان بيان أنواع المنسوخ فإنه سيق للمنّة بإحلال الأزواج الكثيرة له، أو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَتُرْجِي مَنْ تَشَاءُ مِنْهُنَّ وَتُؤْوِي إِلَيْكَ مَنْ تَشَاءُ﴾، وهكذا كل ما أوردوا في نظير نسخ الكتاب بالسنة فقد وجدنا فيه نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب بقطع النظر عن السنة على ما حرّرت في "التفسير الأحمدي". ولما فرغ عن بيان أقسام الناسخ شرع في بيان أقسام المنسوخ من الكتاب فقال: بيان أنواع المنسوخ] والمنسوخ أنواع التلاوة والحكم جميعًا، وهو ما نسخ من القرآن في حياة الرسول عليا بالإنساء كما روي أن سورة الأحزاب كانت تعدل سورة البقرة في ضمن ثلث مائة آية أي الرفع عن القلوب والآن بقيت على ما في المصاحف في ضمن سبعين، آية كما روي أن سورة الطلاق كانت تعدل سورة البقرة، والآن بقيت على ما في المصاحف في ضمن اثني عشر آية.* والحكم دون التلاوة، مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَلِيَ دِين﴾، ونحوه قدر سبعين آية كلها منسوخة بآيات القتال، وقيل: مائة وعشرون آية في باب عدم القتال منسوخة بآيات القتال، أي حكما لا تلاوة أو قوله تعالى إلخ معطوف على قوله : قوله تعالى ومعنى الآية تُرجي أي تطلق من تشاء منهن وتُؤوي أي تمسك إليك من تشاء، وأراد بالإمساك ما يعم النكاح الجديد أيضًا؛ لأنه بسبب الإمساك. كذا قال الحلبي في حاشية "تفسير البيضاوي". (القمر) ما حرّرت إلخ فإن الشارح لله بين هناك نسخ الآية بالآية، وعد الآيات المنسوخة والناسخة. (القمر) من الكتاب: إنما قيّد بهذا؛ لأن الغرض ههنا تقسيم المنسوخ من الكتاب، لا تقسيم المنسوخ مطلقًا كتابًا كان أو سنة، ويصرّح به الشارح له فيما سيجيء بقوله: وإنما خصصنا إلخ. (القمر) التلاوة والحكم أي تلاوة اللفظ والحكم المتعلّق بمعناه . (القمر) حياة الرسول أي لا بعد وفاته كما قد مرّ منّا . (القمر) كما روي أن سورة الأحزاب إلخ كذا أورد العلي القارئ له ناقلا من ابن الملك، وقال الشارح له في "التفسيرات الأحمدية : روي أن سورة الأحزاب كانت مائتي أو ثلث مائة آية، والآن بقي على ما في المصاحف، وهو ثلاث وسبعون آية (القمر) سورة الطلاق كانت إلخ قال الشارح في "التفسيرات الأحمدية" : سورة الطلاق كانت أطول من سورة البقرة. (القمر) وهو ثلاثة هكذا أورده ابن الملك ثم علي القارئ، وأخرج أبو عبيدة في كتابه بسنده إلى أبي بن قال: سورة الأحزاب كانت تعدل سورة البقرة. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٧،٢٦]
Chapter on divisions of Bayan: Explanation of the types of the abrogated. For it was sent as a favor by allowing many wives to him, or His saying, the Exalted: 'You may put aside whom you wish of them and take to yourself whom you wish' (33:51). And similarly, everything they adduced as parallel to abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah, we find in it abrogation of the Book by the Book, disregarding the Sunnah, as I have explained in al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi. And when he finished explaining the divisions of the abrogating, he began explaining the divisions of the abrogated from the Book, saying: Explanation of the types of the abrogated. And the abrogated is of types: recitation and ruling together, and that is what was abrogated from the Quran during the life of the Messenger by way of causing to forget, as it is narrated that Surah al-Ahzab was equivalent to Surah al-Baqarah within a third of a hundred verses, i.e., removal from hearts, and now it remains in the musahif within seventy verses, as it is narrated that Surah al-Talaq was equivalent to Surah al-Baqarah, and now it remains in the musahif within twelve verses. And ruling without recitation, such as His saying: 'For you is your religion, and for me is my religion' (109:6), and similar to it about seventy verses all of which are abrogated by the verses of fighting. And it is said: one hundred and twenty verses concerning non-fighting are abrogated by the verses of fighting, i.e., ruling not recitation. Or His saying etc. is conjoined to His saying. And the meaning of the verse 'you may put aside' meaning you may divorce whom you wish of them, and 'take to yourself' meaning you may keep with you whom you wish. And He intended by keeping what includes new marriage also, because it is due to keeping. Thus said al-Halabi in his marginalia on Tafsir al-Baydawi. (Al-Qamar) 'What I explained etc.' the commentator had there explained the abrogation of verse by verse, and counted the abrogated and abrogating verses. (Al-Qamar) 'From the Book': it is restricted by this because the purpose here is the division of the abrogated from the Book, not the division of the abrogated absolutely, whether Book or Sunnah. And the commentator declares that later in his saying: 'And we only specified etc.' (Al-Qamar) 'Recitation and ruling' i.e., recitation of the wording and the ruling connected to its meaning. (Al-Qamar) 'During the life of the Messenger' i.e., not after his death, as has preceded from us. (Al-Qamar) 'As it is narrated that Surah al-Ahzab etc.' Thus al-‘Ali al-Qari quoted it, transmitting from Ibn al-Malik. And the commentator said in al-Tafsirat al-Ahmadiyya: It is narrated that Surah al-Ahzab was two hundred or a third of a hundred verses, and now it remains in the musahif, and it is seventy-three verses. (Al-Qamar) 'Surah al-Talaq was etc.' The commentator said in al-Tafsirat al-Ahmadiyya: Surah al-Talaq was longer than Surah al-Baqarah. (Al-Qamar) 'And it is three' thus Ibn al-Malik quoted it, then al-‘Ali al-Qari. And Abu Ubaydah narrated in his book with his chain to Ubayy ibn Ka‘b, he said: Surah al-Ahzab was equivalent to Surah al-Baqarah. [Ishraq al-Absar 27,26]
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage defines the two types of abrogated (mansukh) Quranic verses: (1) abrogation of both recitation (tilawah) and ruling (hukm) – where the verse was removed from the Quranic text and its legal ruling is also no longer applicable; examples given are Surah al-Ahzab and Surah al-Talaq, which originally were much longer but were later abrogated in recitation, leaving only shorter versions. (2) abrogation of ruling only without recitation – where the verse remains in the Quran but its legal ruling is replaced; example is the verse of religious tolerance (109:6) abrogated by the verses of fighting (ayat al-qital). The commentator clarifies that this classification is limited to abrogation from the Book, not including abrogation of Sunnah. The discussion also includes references to commentaries and the report from Ubayy ibn Ka‘b about the original length of Surah al-Ahzab.

Key Terms
منسوخ التلاوة والحكم (mansukh al-tilawah wa al-hukm): A verse whose wording and legal ruling are both abrogated, removed from the Quranic text and discontinued in law.
منسوخ الحكم دون التلاوة (mansukh al-hukm duna al-tilawah): A verse that remains in the Quran but its legal ruling is abrogated by a later verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of mansukh does the example of Surah al-Ahzab being reduced in length illustrate?
A) Abrogation of recitation only
B) Abrogation of ruling only
C) Abrogation of both recitation and ruling
D) No abrogation at all

Key Takeaway
The Quranic naskh is of two types: complete removal of word and ruling, or retention of word while the ruling is replaced.

Naskh — Abrogation

The Three Types of Mansukh (Abrogated Verses) in the Quran
Classifies abrogated Quranic verses into three categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a Quranic passage into one of the three types of mansukh and explain the Hanafi evidence for each type.

Core Idea
Quranic abrogation may remove a verse's recitation, its ruling, or both — each type has distinct implications for fiqh.

Having discussed the types of nasikh (abrogating verses), the author now turns to the types of mansukh (abrogated verses). This classification is essential for anyone who works with the Quran to distinguish between what is still legally binding and what is not. The passage provides three clear categories with accompanying examples from the Quran and transmitted reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the passage and list the three types of mansukh: (1) naskh al-tilāwa wa al-ḥukm (both recitation and ruling abrogated), (2) naskh al-ḥukm dūna al-tilāwa (ruling abrogated while recitation remains), (3) naskh al-tilāwa dūna al-ḥukm (recitation abrogated while ruling remains).
The passage also mentions a variant: ziyāda 'alā al-naṣṣ (addition to the text), which some Hanafis consider a form of naskh of the description.
2
Match examples to each type
For each type, find the example given in the passage. Type 1: Surah al-Ahzab and Surah al-Talaq (longer original versions now shortened). Type 2: Verses of tolerance (e.g., 'For you is your religion, for me is mine') abrogated by sword verses. Type 3: The stoning verse (rajm) and Ibn Mas'ud's variant readings (e.g., adding 'consecutive' to fasting verse).
The stoning verse is the classic evidence for naskh al-tilāwa dūna al-ḥukm.
3
Analyze the evidence for each type
For type 3, trace the proof: The hadith of Umar (reported by Malik and the two Shaykhs) stating that the stoning verse was once recited and then its recitation was abrogated while the ruling remained. Identify the operative phrase: 'The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, then stone them.' This shows the ruling's survival despite textual removal.
The Hanafi usul principle: no necessary connection between recitation and ruling; they can be separated.
4
Apply the classification to new scenarios
Given a verse scenario, determine which type of naskh applies. For example: Quran 2:180 (bequest for parents) is still recited but its ruling is replaced by inheritance verses - that is type 2. Quran 24:2 (flogging for fornication) remains both recited and ruling - not abrogated.
Not every verse is subject to naskh; the classification only applies when abrogation has occurred.

فصل في أقسام البيان بيان أنواع المنسوخ فإنه سيق للمنّة بإحلال الأزواج الكثيرة له، أو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَتُرْجِي مَنْ تَشَاءُ مِنْهُنَّ وَتُؤْوِي إِلَيْكَ مَنْ تَشَاءُ﴾ (الأحزاب: ٥١)، وهكذا كل ما أوردوا في نظير نسخ الكتاب بالسنة فقد وجدنا فيه نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب بقطع النظر عن السنة على ما حرّرت في "التفسير الأحمدي". ولما فرغ عن بيان أقسام الناسخ شرع في بيان أقسام المنسوخ من الكتاب فقال: بيان أنواع المنسوخ. والمنسوخ أنواع: التلاوة والحكم جميعًا، وهو ما نسخ من القرآن في حياة الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بالإنساء كما روي أن سورة الأحزاب كانت تعدل سورة البقرة في ضمن ثلث مائة آية أي الرفع عن القلوب والآن بقيت على ما في المصاحف في ضمن سبعين آية، كما روي أن سورة الطلاق كانت تعدل سورة البقرة، والآن بقيت على ما في المصاحف في ضمن اثني عشر آية. والحكم دون التلاوة، مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَلِيَ دِينِ﴾ (الكافرون: ٦) ونحوه قدر سبعين آية كلها منسوخة بآيات القتال، وقيل: مائة وعشرون آية في باب عدم القتال منسوخة بآيات القتال، أي حكما لا تلاوة أو قوله تعالى إلخ معطوف على قوله: قوله تعالى ومعنى الآية تُرجي أي تطلق من تشاء منهن وتُؤوي أي تمسك إليك من تشاء، وأراد بالإمساك ما يعم النكاح الجديد أيضًا؛ لأنه بسبب الإمساك. كذا قال الحلبي في حاشية "تفسير البيضاوي". (القمر) ما حرّرت إلخ فإن الشارح لله بين هناك نسخ الآية بالآية، وعد الآيات المنسوخة والناسخة. (القمر) من الكتاب: إنما قيّد بهذا؛ لأن الغرض ههنا تقسيم المنسوخ من الكتاب، لا تقسيم المنسوخ مطلقًا كتابًا كان أو سنة، ويصرّح به الشارح له فيما سيجيء بقوله: وإنما خصصنا إلخ. (القمر) التلاوة والحكم أي تلاوة اللفظ والحكم المتعلّق بمعناه . (القمر) حياة الرسول أي لا بعد وفاته كما قد مرّ منّا . (القمر) كما روي أن سورة الأحزاب إلخ كذا أورد العلي القارئ له ناقلا من ابن الملك، وقال الشارح له في "التفسيرات الأحمدية: روي أن سورة الأحزاب كانت مائتي أو ثلث مائة آية، والآن بقي على ما في المصاحف، وهو ثلاث وسبعون آية (القمر) سورة الطلاق كانت إلخ قال الشارح في "التفسيرات الأحمدية": سورة الطلاق كانت أطول من سورة البقرة. (القمر) وهو ثلاثة هكذا أورده ابن الملك ثم علي القارئ، وأخرج أبو عبيدة في كتابه بسنده إلى أبي بن قال: سورة الأحزاب كانت تعدل سورة البقرة. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٧،٢٦] وسوى آيات عدم القتال عشرون آية منسوخة التلاوة على رأي صاحب "الإتقان"، وعندي أنها زائدة على عشرين إلى أربعين أو أكثر، وعلم هذا كله فرض على الذي يعمل بالقرآن ليميّز الناسخ من المنسوخ ويعمل بالناسخ دون المنسوخ، وقد بينت كل ذلك بالتفصيل في "التفسير الأحمدي" بما لا يتصور المزيد عليه في كتب أبي حنيفة له وإن بينه الشافعية بأطول في كتبهم. والتلاوة دون الحكم، مثل قوله تعالى: الشيخ والشيخة إذا زَنَيا فارجموهما نَكَالاً مِنَ اللَّهِ وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ، ومثل قراءة ابن مسعود: ﴿فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ﴾ (البقرة: ١٩٦) متتابعات بزيادة "متتابعات" وقوله: "فاقطعوا أيمانهما" مكان قوله "أيديهما". ونسخ وصف في الحكم بأن ينسخ عمومه وإطلاقه ويبقى أصله، وذلك مثل الزيادة على النص (المائدة: ٣٨) منسوخة إلخ هكذا وجدنا عبارة الكتاب في النسخ حتى النسخة التي بخط المصنف له، والظاهر أنه زلّة من قلم الناسخ، والصحيح منسوخة الحكم دون التلاوة؛ لأن الكلام فيه لا في منسوخ التلاوة ويعلم هذا الإتقان أيضًا، فإنه سرد السيوطي له فيه عشرين آيات منسوخة الحكم دون التلاوة، ونظم فيه أبياتا، والعلم علام الغيوب. (القمر) في التفسير الأحمدي: حيث فصل هناك الآيات المنسوخة والناسخة. (القمر) والتلاوة دون الحكم إلخ قال بعض المحققين وأما نسخ أحدهما فقط من الحكم فقط أو التلاوة فقط فيجوز عند الجمهور، ولا تلازم بين جواز التلاوة وحكم المدلول، فيجوز الانفكاك بينهما. (السنبلي) الشيخ والشيخة أي المحصن والمحصنة، وقد مرّ معنى الإحصان، وهذا القول مما كان يُتلى في كتاب الله تعالى، شهد به عمر، كذا في فتح القدير" ثم نسخ تلاوته. (القمر) والله عزيز حكيم إلخ: روى الإمام مالك رضي الله عنه والشيخان عن ابن عباس أن عمر رضي الله عنه قام فحمد الله وأثنى عليه ثم قال: أما بعد أيها الناس، إن الله بعث محمدا بالحق وأنزل عليه الكتاب فكان فيما أنزل عليه آية الرجم قرأناها ووعيناها الشيخ والشيخة إذا زنيا فارجموهما إلخ ورجم رسول الله ورحمنا بعده، فأخشى أن يطول بالناس زمان أن يقول قائل: لا نجد آية الرجم في كتاب الله، فيضلوا بترك فريضة أنزل الله تعالى (السنبلي) قراءة ابن مسعود إلخ: وهذه قراءة مشهورة إلى زمن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه، لكن لم يوجد فيه النقل المتواتر الذي يدور عليه رُحى ثبوت القرآن. (القمر) فمن لم يجد أي إطعام عشرة مساكين وكسوتهم، وتحرير رقبة في كفارة اليمين. (القمر) وقوله أي قول ابن مسعود في حدّ السارق والسارقة، ثم اعلم أنه نسخت تلاوة هاتين القراءتين في حياة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بصرف القلوب عن حفظهما إلا قلب راويهما. (القمر) الزيادة على النص إلخ: قال القاضي أبو زيد: لم يوجد في كتاب الله ما نسخ بالسنة إلا بطريق الزيادة على النص.(السنبلي)
Chapter on the divisions of the explanation: explanation of the types of the abrogated. For it was intended for the favor of permitting many wives to him, or His statement: 'You may defer whom you wish of them and may take to you whom you wish.' And likewise, everything they presented regarding abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah, we found in it abrogation of the Book by the Book, disregarding the Sunnah, as I set down in 'al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi'. And when he finished explaining the divisions of the abrogating, he began explaining the divisions of the abrogated from the Book, saying: explanation of the types of the abrogated. The abrogated are types: (1) the recitation and the ruling together, and it is that which was abrogated from the Quran during the life of the Messenger, peace be upon him, by causing forgetfulness, as it is reported that Surah al-Ahzab was equal to Surah al-Baqarah in length within a third of one hundred verses—i.e., removal from hearts—and now it remains in the codices within seventy verses; as it is reported that Surah al-Talaq was equal to Surah al-Baqarah, and now it remains in the codices within twelve verses. (2) The ruling without the recitation, like His statement: 'For you is your religion, and for me is my religion' and similar to it about seventy verses, all abrogated by the verses of fighting; and it is said: one hundred and twenty verses concerning non-fighting abrogated by verses of fighting—i.e., ruling only, not recitation. Or His statement etc. is conjoined to His statement: His statement and the meaning of the verse 'turji' meaning you divorce whom you wish of them, and 'tu'wi' meaning you keep to yourself whom you wish; and by 'keeping' he meant what includes new marriage as well, because it is through keeping. Thus said al-Halabi in his gloss on 'Tafsir al-Baydawi'. (al-Qamar) 'What I set down' etc.: for the commentator explained there the abrogation of a verse by another verse, and counted the abrogated and abrogating verses. (al-Qamar) 'from the Book': he only restricted it thus because the purpose here is the division of the abrogated from the Book, not the division of the abrogated absolutely, whether Book or Sunnah, as the commentator will make clear later by his saying 'we only specified' etc. (al-Qamar) 'the recitation and the ruling' i.e., the recitation of the wording and the ruling related to its meaning. (al-Qamar) 'life of the Messenger' i.e., not after his death as has passed from us. (al-Qamar) 'as it is reported that Surah al-Ahzab' etc.: thus narrated al-Qari from Ibn al-Malik, and the commentator said in 'al-Tafsirat al-Ahmadiyya': it is reported that Surah al-Ahzab was two hundred or a third of one hundred verses, and now it remains in the codices, which is seventy-three verses. (al-Qamar) 'Surah al-Talaq was' etc.: the commentator said in 'al-Tafsirat al-Ahmadiyya': Surah al-Talaq was longer than Surah al-Baqarah. (al-Qamar) 'and it is three': thus narrated Ibn al-Malik and then Ali al-Qari, and Abu Ubaydah narrated in his book with his chain to Ubayy that he said: Surah al-Ahzab was equal to Surah al-Baqarah. [Ishraq al-Absar 27,26] And besides the verses of non-fighting, twenty verses of abrogated recitation according to the author of al-Itqan, and in my view they exceed twenty to forty or more. And knowledge of all this is an obligation upon whoever works with the Quran to distinguish the abrogating from the abrogated and act upon the abrogating not the abrogated. I have explained all that in detail in 'al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi' in a way that no addition is conceivable in the books of Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, although the Shafi'is have explained it at length in their books. (3) The recitation without the ruling, like His statement: 'The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, then stone them as a punishment from Allah, and Allah is Mighty, Wise'; and like the reading of Ibn Mas'ud: 'And whoever cannot find [a sacrifice], then a fast of three days' with the addition 'consecutive', and his statement: 'then cut off their hands' instead of His statement 'their hands'. And abrogation of a description in the ruling by abrogating its generality and absoluteness while its origin remains, and that is like the addition to the text (al-Ma'idah: 38). 'Abrogated' etc.: thus we found the wording of the book in the copies, even in a copy in the author's own hand, and it appears that it is a slip of the scribe's pen; the correct is 'abrogated in ruling without recitation' because the discussion is about that, not about abrogated recitation. And this is also known from al-Itqan, for al-Suyuti compiled therein twenty verses abrogated in ruling without recitation, and composed verses on them. And Allah knows all hidden things. (al-Qamar) 'in al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi': where he detailed there the abrogated and abrogating verses. (al-Qamar) 'The recitation without the ruling' etc.: some researchers said: as for the abrogation of only one of them—only the ruling or only the recitation—it is permissible according to the majority, and there is no necessary connection between the permissibility of the recitation and the ruling of the indication, so disconnection between them is permissible. (al-Sunbuli) 'The old man and the old woman' i.e., the muhsan and muhsana, and the meaning of ihsan has passed; this statement was among what was recited in the Book of Allah, witnessed by 'Umar, as in Fath al-Qadir, then its recitation was abrogated. (al-Qamar) 'And Allah is Mighty, Wise' etc.: Imam Malik and the two Shaykhs reported from Ibn Abbas that 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, stood and praised Allah and then said: O people, indeed Allah sent Muhammad with the truth and revealed to him the Book; among what He revealed was the verse of stoning; we recited it and understood it: 'The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, then stone them' etc. And the Messenger of Allah stoned and we stoned after him; so I fear that with time a person will say: We do not find the verse of stoning in the Book of Allah, and thus they will go astray by abandoning a duty Allah revealed. (al-Sunbuli) 'the reading of Ibn Mas'ud' etc.: And this reading was well-known up to the time of Abu Hanifa, but there is no mutawatir transmission upon which the foundation of the Quran's authenticity revolves. (al-Qamar) 'And whoever cannot find' i.e., feeding ten poor people and clothing them, and freeing a slave in atonement for an oath. (al-Qamar) 'and his statement' i.e., the statement of Ibn Mas'ud concerning the limit of the male and female thief. Then know that the recitation of these two readings was abrogated during the life of the Prophet, peace be upon him, by turning hearts away from memorizing them except the heart of their transmitter. (al-Qamar) 'the addition to the text' etc.: al-Qadi Abu Zaid said: There is nothing in the Book of Allah that was abrogated by the Sunnah except by way of addition to the text. (al-Sunbuli)
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage is a division of mansukh (abrogated) into three categories. It begins by clarifying that the discussion is limited to abrogation within the Quran (not Sunnah). The first type is abrogation of both recitation (tilaawah) and ruling (hukm), where the verse was removed from the Quran entirely during the Prophet's lifetime through forgetfulness caused by Allah. Examples include Surah al-Ahzab and Surah al-Talaq, which were originally as long as Surah al-Baqarah but remain much shorter now. The second type is abrogation of the ruling only, while the recitation remains. The classic example is the verse of stoning (rajm) for married adulterers, which used to be recited but is no longer part of the Quran; however, its ruling still applies. Similarly, verses of tolerance like 'For you is your religion' were abrogated by the sword verses. The third type is abrogation of recitation only, where the ruling remains but the text is removed. Examples include the additional phrase 'consecutive' in Ibn Mas'ud's reading of the fasting verse, and 'cut off their hands' instead of 'their hands' in the theft verse. The passage also discusses an addition to the text (ziyada 'ala al-nass), which some Hanafi scholars consider a form of abrogation of the description (wasf) without affecting the essence. The author emphasizes that distinguishing these types is obligatory for anyone working with the Quran, and he has elaborated in his own work al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi. He notes that the Shafi'is discuss this at greater length, but the Hanafi position is presented here. The discussion includes references to known hadith about Umar's testimony regarding the stoning verse and Ibn Mas'ud's variant readings that were abrogated.

Key Terms
منسوخ (mansūkh): The abrogated; a verse whose legal ruling or recitation (or both) has been removed by a later verse or Sunnah.
ناسخ (nāsikh): The abrogating; the later verse or Sunnah that removes the ruling or recitation of an earlier one.
نسخ التلاوة والحكم (naskh al-tilāwa wa al-ḥukm): Abrogation of both recitation and ruling; the verse is completely removed from the Quran and its ruling no longer applies.
نسخ الحكم دون التلاوة (naskh al-ḥukm dūna al-tilāwa): Abrogation of the ruling while the recitation remains; the verse is still recited but its ruling is no longer in effect.
نسخ التلاوة دون الحكم (naskh al-tilāwa dūna al-ḥukm): Abrogation of recitation while the ruling remains; the verse is removed from the Quran but its ruling continues to apply.
الزيادة على النص (al-ziyāda 'alā al-naṣṣ): An addition to a text that abrogates the original ruling's generality or absoluteness while preserving its core.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of naskh is exemplified by the verse of stoning (rajm), which is no longer in the Quran but its ruling is still to be applied?
A) Abrogation of both recitation and ruling
B) Abrogation of ruling only, recitation remains
C) Abrogation of recitation only, ruling remains
D) Abrogation of the description in the ruling

Key Takeaway
Abrogation in the Quran is of three types: of recitation only, of ruling only, or of both; knowing which applies is essential for correct legal derivation.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate

Examples of Naskh al-Tilawah: Verse of Stoning and Ibn Mas'ud's Readings
Examples of naskh al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify examples of naskh al-tilawah and explain why their recitation is abrogated while the ruling remains, using the Hanafi usul framework.

Core Idea
Some Quranic verses were abrogated in recitation but their rulings remain in force.

The concept of naskh is crucial for understanding how certain rulings persist despite changes in the Quranic text. In this lesson, we examine two concrete examples from the Hanafi usul tradition: the so-called 'verse of stoning' and the variant readings of Ibn Mas'ud. These illustrate how a text can be removed from the Quran (tilawah) while its legal effect continues through other evidence like Sunnah and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of naskh
The passage explicitly introduces 'al-tilawah duna al-hukm' – abrogation of recitation without abrogation of the ruling. Understand the distinction between this and other types of naskh (e.g., abrogation of both recitation and ruling, or ruling only).
This is a key Hanafi usul category; not all madhhabs agree on its occurrence.
2
Examine the first example: verse of stoning
The text quotes what was once a Quranic verse: 'The old man and the old woman, when they commit adultery, stone them...' Although this is no longer in the Quran, the ruling of stoning for married adulterers is established by the Sunnah (mutawatir hadith) and ijma' of the Companions.
The evidence for its original Quranic status comes from testimonies like that of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA).
3
Examine the second example: Ibn Mas'ud's readings
The reading of Ibn Mas'ud includes the word 'consecutively' (mutatabi'at) in the fasting verse (2:196). Similarly, his reading says 'cut off their right hands' instead of 'their hands' in the theft verse (5:38). These variants lack tawatur (mass transmission), so they are considered abrogated in recitation. The legal implications, such as the obligation of consecutive fasting, may still be supported by other evidence.
These readings are classified as shadhdh (irregular) by the majority.
4
Understand the Hanafi position on such readings
Hanafi usul accepts naskh al-tilawah as valid. The rationale: the recitation was abrogated to preserve the Quranic text's integrity, but the ruling remains binding because it is independently established. This illustrates how multiple sources (Quran, Sunnah, ijma) interact.
The Shafi'i school also accepts this type but differs on the number of examples (e.g., they do not count Ibn Mas'ud's readings as naskh al-tilawah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتلاوة دون الحكم، مثل قوله تعالى : الشيخ والشيخة إذا زَنَيا فارجموهما نَكَالاً مِنَ اللَّهِ وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ، ومثل قراءة ابن مسعود : ﴿ فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ » (البقرة : ١٩٦) متتابعات بزيادة "متتابعات" وقوله : "فاقطعوا أيمانهما" مكان قوله "أيديهما".
And recitation without the ruling, such as His statement, the Exalted: 'The old man and the old woman, when they commit adultery, stone them as a punishment from Allah, and Allah is Mighty, Wise.' And such as the reading of Ibn Mas'ud: 'And whoever does not find [a sacrifice] then fasting three days' [al-Baqarah 2:196] with the addition of 'consecutively', and his statement: 'cut off their right hands' instead of 'their hands'.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage lists examples of naskh al-tilawah (abrogation of recitation without abrogation of the ruling). The first example is the so-called 'verse of stoning' (āyat al-rajm), which was once part of the Quran but whose recitation was abrogated. The ruling of stoning for married adulterers, however, remains in force according to the consensus of the Companions. The second example is the reading of Ibn Mas'ud which includes the word 'consecutively' (mutatābi'āt) in the verse about fasting for one who cannot afford a sacrifice; this addition was recited but later abrogated in recitation. Similarly, his reading of 'cut off their right hands' instead of 'their hands' in the verse of theft (al-Mā'idah 5:38) was also abrogated in recitation. In Hanafi usul, such readings are considered abrogated in recitation because they lack tawātur (mass transmission), though their legal implications may still be considered (e.g., the obligation of consecutive fasting in certain cases through other evidence).

Key Terms
التلاوة دون الحكم (al-tilāwah dūna al-ḥukm): When the recited text is abrogated but the legal ruling continues to be valid.
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as a punishment for married adulterers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of naskh is exemplified by the verse of stoning?
A) Naskh al-hukm wa al-tilawah
B) Naskh al-tilawah alone
C) Naskh al-hukm alone
D) No naskh

Key Takeaway
Naskh al-tilawah removes the recitation of a verse from the Quran but preserves its legal ruling, which must be supported by other evidence.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate

Ziyada ala al-Nass: Naskh or Bayan?
Explains ziyada ala al-nass and the Hanafi-Shafi'i split

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis classify adding a condition or ruling (ziyada) to a Quranic text via Sunnah as naskh, contrast the Shafi'i view, and apply this distinction to the examples of wiping over khuffs and adding exile to flogging.

Core Idea
Adding to a Quranic ruling via Sunnah is naskh for Hanafis, requiring mutawatir; for Shafi'is it is takhsis, allowing khabar wahid.

This lesson unpacks a foundational usul dispute: when a hadith adds a condition (like wiping over khuffs) to a Quranic command (washing feet), is that abrogation (naskh) or clarification (bayan)? The Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools differ sharply on this, with major consequences for which sources can modify the Quran. The passage uses three concrete examples: the khuff wiping rule, the addition of exile to flogging for unmarried fornicators, and the condition of faith in expiations via qiyas. By understanding these, you will grasp the Hanafi insistence on high certainty for any change to the revealed text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
What is the legal nature of adding an extra element (ruling, condition) to a Quranic text by another source (Sunnah)? Is it naskh (abrogation) or bayan/takhsis (clarification)?
Naskh replaces the original ruling; bayan specifies the original intent.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Proof
Hanafis say it is naskh. The Quran commanded absolute washing of feet; the hadith added the condition of not wearing khuffs, thus abrogating the absoluteness. Since naskh lifts an existing ruling, it requires evidence of equal or higher certainty (mutawatir or mashhur).
The hadith about khuffs is considered mashhur, thus sufficient for naskh.
3
State the Shafi‘i Position and Proof
Shafi‘is say it is takhsis and bayan. The Quranic command was always intended for those not in a state of khuff, but the specification was revealed later. This is not abrogation but clarification, so any authentic evidence (khabar wahid, qiyas) can specify the general.
For Shafi‘is, the hadith does not change the ruling but merely explains its scope.
4
Analyze the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The dispute affects whether khabar wahid or qiyas can add to the Quran. Example: adding exile to flogging for unmarried fornicators. Hanafis reject because the hadith is khabar wahid and cannot abrogate; Shafi‘is accept as bayan. Another example: adding the condition of faith in expiation for oaths via qiyas to killing expiation.
Hanafis maintain the Quranic penalty is only flogging; exile is optional policy (siyasa).
5
Conclude with the Hanafi Tarjih Reasoning
The passage implies the Hanafi view is stronger: naskh requires certainty, and khabar wahid and qiyas lack that certainty. Treating addition as bayan weakens the stability of the revealed text. The Hanafi position upholds the principle that only sure evidence can override the apparent meaning of the Quran.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on usul al-thubut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام البيان بيان أنواع المنسوخ كزيادة مسح الخفين على غسل الرجلين الثابت بالكتاب، فإن الكتاب يقتضي أن يكون الغسل هو الوظيفة للرجلين، سواء كان متحققا أو لا، والحديث المشهور نسخ هذا الإطلاق وقال : إنما الغسل إذا لم يكن لابس الخفين فالآن صار الغسل بعض الوظيفة. عندنا فإنها نسخ وعند الشافعي حبه تخصیص، وبيان فلا يجوز عندنا إلا بالخبر المتواتر أو المشهور كسائر النسخ، وعنده يجوز بخبر الواحد والقياس كباقي البيان. حتى أثبت زيادة النفي على الجلد بخبر الواحد، وهو قوله عليه: "البكر بالبكر جلد مائة وتغريب عام" فإنه خبر واحد يجوز الزيادة به على الكتاب الدال على الجلد فقط عنده. وزيادة قيد الإيمان في كفارة اليمين والظهار بالقياس على كفارة القتل المقيّدة بالإيمان، فإنه يجوز
Chapter on the divisions of Bayan: Explanation of the types of the abrogated, such as the addition of wiping over khuffs to the washing of the feet established by the Book. For the Book necessitates that washing is the duty for the feet, whether one is wearing khuffs or not. The famous hadith abrogated this absoluteness and said: 'Washing is only when one is not wearing khuffs.' So now washing becomes part of the duty. According to us, this is naskh; according to al-Shafi‘i, it is takhsis and bayan. Thus it is not permissible according to us except with mutawatir or mashhur khabar like other naskh. According to him, it is permissible with khabar wahid and qiyas like other bayan. So much so that he established the addition of exile to flogging with khabar wahid, namely his statement, peace be upon him: 'The unmarried with the unmarried: one hundred lashes and exile for a year.' For it is a khabar wahid by which he permits addition to the Book which only indicates flogging. And the addition of the condition of faith in the expiation for an oath and zihar by analogy to the expiation for killing which is restricted by faith is permissible.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal nature of adding extra conditions or rulings to Quranic texts through the Sunnah (ziyada ala al-nass). The example given is the obligation of washing the feet in wudu from the Quran (al-Ma'idah 5:6) versus the hadith that only requires washing when not wearing khuffs; instead, wiping over khuffs is permitted. For Hanafis, this addition abrogates the absolute Quranic command, because it restricts a general rule. For Shafi'is, it is not naskh but takhsis (specification) and bayan (clarification), meaning the original text always intended this limitation, but it was clarified later. Consequently, Hanafis require the abrogating evidence to be of equal or higher certainty (mutawatir or mashhur), as naskh cannot be accomplished by speculative reports. Shafi'is, treating it as bayan, accept khabar wahid and qiyas. The passage also cites the addition of exile (taghrib) to flogging for unmarried fornicators, based on a hadith that Shafi'is use to add to the Quranic punishment of flogging only (Surah al-Nur). Hanafis reject this addition as naskh by khabar wahid, which is invalid. They maintain that the Quranic punishment is only flogging; exile is permissible only if the ruler deems it as policy (siyasa), not as part of the fixed punishment. Similarly, the addition of the condition of faith (iman) in expiation (kaffarah) for oaths and zihar (a form of divorce) is argued by Shafi'is through qiyas to the expiation for accidental killing, which explicitly requires freeing a believing slave. Hanafis reject this because it would be naskh by qiyas, which is impermissible. This dispute illustrates the Hanafi insistence on strict textual certainty for any departure from the apparent meaning of the Quran.

Key Terms
الزيادة على النص (al-ziyāda ‘alā al-naṣṣ): Adding a new legal element (condition, ruling, etc.) to a Quranic text via a source of law.
التخصيص (al-takhṣīṣ): Specifying the general meaning of a text by another evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the addition of exile to flogging for unmarried fornicators not accepted?
A) Because the hadith is not authentic
B) Because the Quran does not mention exile, and adding it would be naskh, which requires mutawatir or mashhur evidence, but the hadith is khabar wahid
C) Because exile is not a fixed punishment in Islam
D) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school insists that adding any condition or ruling to the Quran via Sunnah is naskh, demanding the highest level of transmission (tawatur or shuhra) to protect the certainty of the divine text.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
15 min
Increase Upon a Text: Naskh or Takhsis? The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Usul dispute on whether ziyada is naskh or takhsis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis treat ziyada as naskh, contrast the Shafi'i view, and apply the rule that only mutawatir/mashhur evidence can abrogate a definitive text.

Core Idea
Increase upon a text is abrogation, not specification: only definitive evidence can lift a definitive ruling.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar addresses a fundamental usul dispute: when a later text adds a condition or ruling to an earlier text, does it abrogate the earlier (naskh) or merely specify its scope (takhsis)? The Hanafi school insists it is naskh, requiring strong evidence; the Shafi'is see it as takhsis, allowing weaker proofs. We will examine the arguments, examples, and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What is ziyada (increase)? The passage defines it as adding a condition or pillar to a textual ruling. The disagreement is whether this addition lifts the original ruling (naskh) or clarifies its scope (takhsis).
Ziyada can be a condition (shart) or pillar (rukn) added to a ruling.
2
State the Hanafi position
Hanafis hold that ziyada is naskh because it changes the earlier ruling. Therefore, it requires the same level of evidence as naskh: mutawatir or mashhur transmission. Khabar wahid and qiyas are insufficient.
The example of wiping over khuff: the hadith is mashhur, so it can abrogate the Quranic washing requirement.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Shafi'is consider ziyada as takhsis (specification) – the original ruling always included the exception, but it was not yet clarified. Thus, any evidence that can specify (khabar wahid, qiyas) is valid for ziyada.
They view the hadith on wiping over khuff as specifying that the washing command applies only when not wearing khuff.
4
Examine the examples
Three examples are given: (1) wiping over khuff vs. washing feet; (2) addition of exile to flogging for unmarried fornicators; (3) adding the condition of faith to expiation slaves via qiyas. For each, apply both schools' principles to see the difference.
The second example is key: Hanafis reject the exile addition because it uses khabar wahid, while Shafi'is accept it.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that Hanafis do not include exile in the hadd punishment for unmarried fornicators, while Shafi'is do. Also, Hanafis do not require faith in expiation slaves via qiyas; Shafi'is do.
Hanafis allow the imam to impose exile as a discretionary policy (siyasa), not as part of the hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام البيان كزيادة بيان أنواع المنسوخ مسح الخفين على غسل الرجلين الثابت بالكتاب، فإن الكتاب يقتضي أن يكون الغسل هو الوظيفة للرجلين، سواء كان متحققا أو لا، والحديث المشهور نسخ هذا الإطلاق وقال : إنما الغسل إذا لم يكن لابس الخفين فالآن صار الغسل بعض الوظيفة. عندنا فإنها نسخ وعند الشافعي فهي تخصيص وبيان فلا يجوز عندنا إلا بالخبر المتواتر أو المشهور كسائر النسخ، وعنده يجوز بخبر الواحد والقياس كباقي البيان. حتى أثبت زيادة النفي على الجلد بخبر الواحد، وهو قوله عليه: "البكر بالبكر جلد مائة أي تغريب عام وتغريب عام فإنه خبر واحد يجوز الزيادة به على الكتاب الدال على الجلد فقط عنده. وزيادة قيد الإيمان في كفارة اليمين والظهار بالقياس على كفارة القتل المقيّدة بالإيمان، فإنه يجوز أي خطأ على النص: أي النص المطلق بأن يثبت أمر آخر زائد على الحكم المنصوص شرطًا كانت تلك الزيادة أو ركنا. (القمر) الوظيفة إلخ ما يقدر من عمل وطعام ورزق وغير ذلك، والعهد والشرط يقال بينهما وظيفة، أي عهد وشرط جمع وظائف ووظف وربما استعملت الوظيفة بمعنى المنصب والخدمة والمعينة. "أقرب الموارد". (السنبلي) فإنها نسخ عندنا فإن هذه الزيادة رفع حكم إطلاق النص، وهذا الحكم حكم شرعي ارتفع، فصار منسوخا. (القمر) تخصيص وبيان فإن المراد كان من الابتداء وبدو الأمر حكم النص مع هذه الزيادة لكنه لم يبين، وقد بين مع هذا الزمان. (القمر) حتى أثبت إلخ وعندنا لما كان هذه الزيادة نسخًا، ونسخ الكتاب القطعي بخبر الواحد الظني لا يجوز فلا تحكم بهذه الزيادة (القمر) على الجلد أي الذي هو في حد زنا الغير المحصن.(القمر) يجوز الزيادة إلخ ونحن نقول: إن هذا الحديث كان في ابتداء الإسلام ثم نزل آية الجلد أي قوله تعالى: الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ (النور: ۲) فهذه الآية صارت ناسخة لهذا الحديث في باب الزيادة تغريب العام؛ لأن تمام الحدّ في الآية هذا الجلد لا غيرُ ، فليس التغريب من تمام الحد، نعم، إذا رأى الإمام المصلحة في التغريب حكم به سياسةً، وهذا أمر آخر، كذا قيل. (القمر) فإنه يجوز إلخ فالرّقية في كفارة القتل خطاً مقيدة بقيد الإيمان، وفي كفارة اليمين والظهار مطلقة، فالشافعي ليه حمل رقبة هاتين الكفارتين على رقبة كفارة ،القتل وقيدها بالإيمان؛ لأن الكفارات جنس واحد. (القمر) قد ورد في ورد في مسح الخفين أحاديث كثيرة، قال علي القاري لله وردت عن قريب من ثلثين صحابيا، وهو متواتر ،المعنى ومشهور بالاتفاق . [إشراق الأبصار ٢٧] تخريجه .
Chapter on the divisions of bayan (clarification). Like increase. Explanation of the types of abrogated: wiping over khuffain (leather socks) over washing the feet established by the Book, for the Book requires that washing is the function for the feet, whether it is realized or not, and the famous hadith abrogated this absoluteness and said: 'Washing is only when not wearing khuffain,' so now washing became part of the function. According to us, it is abrogation, and according to al-Shafi'i, it is specification and clarification. So according to us, it is not permissible except with mutawatir or mashhur khabar, like other abrogations. According to him, it is permissible with khabar al-wahid and qiyas, like the rest of bayan. Until he established the increase of exile upon flogging with khabar al-wahid, which is his statement (peace be upon him): 'The virgin for the virgin: flogging of one hundred and exile of one year,' and it is khabar wahid, and he permits increase upon the Book which indicates only flogging. And the increase of the condition of faith in the expiation for oath and zihar (declaration of zihar) by qiyas upon the expiation for unintentional killing which is restricted by faith, so it is permissible. (Error) on the text: i.e., the absolute text, by establishing another matter additional to the ruled-upon ruling, whether that increase is a condition or a pillar. (Qamar) 'al-wazifa' etc.: what is estimated of work, food, sustenance, etc., and covenant and condition are called wazifa between them, i.e., covenant and condition. Plural: waza'if and wazif. Sometimes wazifa is used in the sense of position, service, and appointed stipend. 'Aqrab al-Mawarid'. (al-Sanbali) It is abrogation according to us, for this increase lifts the ruling of the absoluteness of the text, and this ruling is a legal ruling that is lifted, so it becomes abrogated. (Qamar) Specification and clarification: for the intended from the beginning and the start of the matter was the ruling of the text with this increase, but it was not clarified, and it was clarified at this time. (Qamar) 'Hatta athbata' etc.: And according to us, since this increase is abrogation, and abrogation of the definitive Book with a speculative khabar wahid is not permissible, so this increase is not ruled upon. (Qamar) 'ala al-jald': i.e., which is in the hadd of zina of the non-muhsan. (Qamar) 'yajuzu al-ziyada' etc.: And we say: This hadith was at the beginning of Islam, then the verse of flogging was revealed, i.e., His statement: 'The fornicatress and fornicator, flog each one of them one hundred lashes' (Surah al-Nur: 2). So this verse abrogated this hadith in the matter of the increase of the exile of the year; because the complete hadd in the verse is this flogging only, not otherwise. So exile is not part of the hadd. Yes, if the imam sees an interest in exile, he may rule by it as policy, and this is another matter. So it is said. (Qamar) 'fainnahu yajuzu' etc.: So the slave in the expiation for unintentional killing is restricted by the condition of faith, while in the expiation for oath and zihar it is unrestricted. So al-Shafi'i carried the slave of these two expiations upon the slave of the expiation for killing and restricted it by faith, because expiations are one genre. (Qamar) Many ahadith have been narrated on wiping over khuffain. Ali al-Qari said: They have been narrated from nearly thirty Companions, and it is mutawatir in meaning and mashhur by agreement. [Ishraq al-Absar 27] Its takhrij.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage deals with a key usul dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is: whether an increase (ziyada) upon a textual ruling constitutes abrogation (naskh) or specification (takhsis). The Hanafi position is that it is naskh because the original ruling is lifted. The Shafi'i position is that it is takhsis because the original intent always included the increase, but it was merely clarified later. The consequence: Hanafis require mutawatir or mashhur evidence for such increases, while Shafi'is accept khabar al-wahid and qiyas. The author provides examples: the hadith limiting ablution to wiping over socks abrogates the Quranic verse about washing feet; the addition of exile in the hadith of flogging for unmarried fornicators; and the use of qiyas to require faith in expiation slaves. The textual hierarchy is that definitive texts (Quran) can only be abrogated by definitive or widely transmitted reports, not speculative ones.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyada): An additional ruling or condition attached to a textual ruling.
النسخ (al-naskh): Lifting a legal ruling by a later evidence.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Specifying a general ruling by evidence that clarifies intent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what type of evidence is required to establish an increase (ziyada) upon a Quranic text?
A) Khabar al-wahid
B) Qiyas
C) Mutawatir or mashhur hadith
D) Any hadith

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats any increase upon a definitive text as abrogation (naskh) that requires equally definitive evidence, while the Shafi'i school treats it as specification (takhsis) permissible with weaker proofs.
